Let's set up coordinates:

Let M = (0,0), N = (d,0). Let ╬®: x^2+y^2 = r^2. ╬ō: (x-d)^2+y^2 = R^2.

Let A = (a, h) with h>0. Then a^2+h^2 = r^2, (a-d)^2+h^2 = R^2.

From these, we derived a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d). And h^2 = r^2 - a^2.

Now define:

p_x = (d+R-r)/2.
p_y = - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h).

We also have v = (p_x - a, p_y - h). Let's compute v explicitly.

First, compute p_x - a = (d+R-r)/2 - a = (d+R-r - 2a)/2.

We know a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d). So 2a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/d. So p_x - a = (d+R-r - (d^2+r^2-R^2)/d)/2 = ( (d(d+R-r) - (d^2+r^2-R^2) )/(2d) ) = ( (d^2+dR-dr - d^2 - r^2 + R^2)/(2d) ) = ( (dR - dr - r^2 + R^2)/(2d) ) = ( (d(R-r) + (R^2 - r^2))/(2d) ) = ( (d(R-r) + (R-r)(R+r))/(2d) ) = ( (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d) ).

So p_x - a = (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d). That's positive since R>r, d>0, R+r>0.

Now compute p_y - h = - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h) - h = - [ (r+a)(d+R-r) + 2h^2 ]/(2h). But we can simplify using h^2 = r^2 - a^2. And also (r+a)(d+R-r) = (r+a)(d+R-r). We might want to express p_y - h in terms of known.

Compute (r+a)(d+R-r) + 2h^2 = (r+a)(d+R-r) + 2(r^2 - a^2) = (r+a)(d+R-r) + 2(r-a)(r+a) = (r+a)[(d+R-r) + 2(r-a)] = (r+a)[d+R-r+2r-2a] = (r+a)[d+R+r-2a].

Thus p_y - h = - (r+a)(d+R+r-2a)/(2h).

Now d+R+r-2a = d+R+r - 2a. But we have a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d). So 2a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/d. Then d+R+r-2a = d+R+r - (d^2+r^2-R^2)/d = (d(d+R+r) - (d^2+r^2-R^2))/d = (d^2+dR+dr - d^2 - r^2 + R^2)/d = (dR+dr - r^2 + R^2)/d = (d(R+r) + (R^2 - r^2))/d = (d(R+r) + (R-r)(R+r))/d = (R+r)(d+R-r)/d.

Thus d+R+r-2a = (R+r)(d+R-r)/d.

So p_y - h = - (r+a) * ((R+r)(d+R-r)/d) / (2h) = - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2dh).

So v = ( v_x, v_y ) where:

v_x = (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d).
v_y = - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2dh).

Now note that v_y is negative (since all factors positive). So v points downward and rightward (v_x positive). So direction of AP is from A to P, which is downward-right.

But p_y = - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h). So p_y negative. Then y_H = ((d+R-r)(d-R+r))/(4 * ( - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h) )) = ((d+R-r)(d-R+r))/(4) * ( -2h/( (r+a)(d+R-r) )) = - (d-R+r) * h / (2(r+a)). Cancel (d+R-r). So y_H = - h (d-R+r) / (2(r+a)).

Now note that d-R+r = d - (R - r). Since d > R - r, this is positive. So y_H negative.

Thus H = ( (d+R-r)/2 , - h (d-R+r)/(2(r+a)) ).

Another idea: Use coordinate geometry but try to compute the condition for tangency in a more algebraic way, perhaps by showing that the line Ōäō is the polar of H with respect to circle (BEF). If we can show that H lies on the polar of something, then the line Ōäō is the polar of H? Alternatively, we can compute the equation of circle (BEF) and then compute the distance from its center to Ōäō and compare with radius. That is a straightforward but heavy computation. Let's attempt to do it systematically, using algebraic simplifications.

We have parameters: d, r, R. We'll treat them as real numbers with R > r > 0, and R - r < d < R + r.

Define:

a = (d^2 + r^2 - R^2)/(2d).
h^2 = r^2 - a^2.

We also have p_x = (d+R-r)/2.
p_y = - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h).

We have v = (v_x, v_y) with:

v_x = (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d).
v_y = - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2dh).

Now we need t_E = -2(A┬Ęv)/(v┬Ęv). Compute A┬Ęv = a v_x + h v_y.

Compute a v_x = a * (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d). And h v_y = h * ( - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2dh) ) = - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2d). So A┬Ęv = a (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d) - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2d) = (1/(2d)) [ a(R-r)(d+R+r) - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r) ].

Simplify inside: Let's denote X = a(R-r)(d+R+r) - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r). Expand both terms.

First term: a(R-r)(d+R+r) = a(R-r)d + a(R-r)(R+r) = a d (R-r) + a (R^2 - r^2).

Second term: (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r) = (r+a)(R+r)d + (r+a)(R+r)(R-r) = (r+a)(R+r)d + (r+a)(R^2 - r^2). So X = a d (R-r) + a (R^2 - r^2) - (r+a)(R+r)d - (r+a)(R^2 - r^2) = a d (R-r) - (r+a)(R+r)d + a (R^2 - r^2) - (r+a)(R^2 - r^2) = d[ a(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] + (R^2 - r^2)[ a - (r+a) ] = d[ a(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] + (R^2 - r^2)(-r) = d[ a(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] - r(R^2 - r^2).

Now compute a(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) = aR - a r - (r+a)R - (r+a)r = aR - a r - rR - aR - r^2 - a r = -2a r - rR - r^2? Wait: aR - aR cancel. So we have -a r - rR - a r - r^2? Actually (r+a)(R+r) = rR + r^2 + aR + a r. So a(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) = aR - a r - rR - r^2 - aR - a r = -2a r - rR - r^2. So that simplifies to -r(2a + R + r). So X = d[ -r(2a + R + r) ] - r(R^2 - r^2) = -r d (2a + R + r) - r(R^2 - r^2) = -r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ].

Thus A┬Ęv = (1/(2d)) * ( -r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ] ) = -r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ]/(2d).

Now we need v┬Ęv = v_x^2+v_y^2. Compute v_x^2 = ((R-r)^2 (d+R+r)^2)/(4d^2). v_y^2 = ((r+a)^2 (R+r)^2 (d+R-r)^2)/(4d^2 h^2). So v┬Ęv = (1/(4d^2))[ (R-r)^2 (d+R+r)^2 + (r+a)^2 (R+r)^2 (d+R-r)^2 / h^2 ].

We also need t_E = -2(A┬Ęv)/(v┬Ęv) = -2 * ( -r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ]/(2d) ) / (v┬Ęv) = ( r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ]/d ) / (v┬Ęv) = r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ]/(d v┬Ęv).

So t_E = r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ]/(d v┬Ęv).

Now E = A + t_E v. So coordinates: E = (a + t_E v_x, h + t_E v_y). Similarly, F = A + t_F v, with t_F = -2(A-N)┬Ęv/(v┬Ęv). Compute A-N = (a-d, h). Then (A-N)┬Ęv = (a-d)v_x + h v_y.

Compute (a-d)v_x = (a-d)*(R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d). And h v_y = - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2d). So (A-N)┬Ęv = (1/(2d))[ (a-d)(R-r)(d+R+r) - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r) ].

Simplify inside: Let Y = (a-d)(R-r)(d+R+r) - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r). Expand:

First term: (a-d)(R-r)(d+R+r) = (a-d)(R-r)d + (a-d)(R-r)(R+r) = (a-d)d(R-r) + (a-d)(R^2 - r^2).

Second term: (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r) = (r+a)(R+r)d + (r+a)(R+r)(R-r) = (r+a)(R+r)d + (r+a)(R^2 - r^2).

So Y = (a-d)d(R-r) + (a-d)(R^2 - r^2) - (r+a)(R+r)d - (r+a)(R^2 - r^2) = d[ (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] + (R^2 - r^2)[ (a-d) - (r+a) ] = d[ (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] + (R^2 - r^2)(a-d - r - a) = d[ (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] + (R^2 - r^2)(-d - r) = d[ (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] - (R^2 - r^2)(d+r).

Now compute (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r). Expand: (a-d)(R-r) = aR - a r - dR + d r. (r+a)(R+r) = rR + r^2 + aR + a r. So difference = aR - a r - dR + d r - rR - r^2 - aR - a r = -2a r - dR + d r - rR - r^2 = -2a r - dR + d r - rR - r^2. Group terms: = -dR + d r - rR - r^2 - 2a r = d(r-R) - r(R+r) - 2a r = -d(R-r) - r(R+r) - 2a r. So (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) = -[ d(R-r) + r(R+r) + 2a r ].

Thus Y = d * ( -[ d(R-r) + r(R+r) + 2a r ] ) - (R^2 - r^2)(d+r) = -d[ d(R-r) + r(R+r) + 2a r ] - (R-r)(R+r)(d+r) = -d^2(R-r) - d r(R+r) - 2a r d - (R-r)(R+r)(d+r).

So Y = -d^2(R-r) - d r(R+r) - 2a r d - (R^2 - r^2)(d+r).

Thus (A-N)┬Ęv = Y/(2d) = -[ d^2(R-r) + d r(R+r) + 2a r d + (R^2 - r^2)(d+r) ]/(2d).

Now t_F = -2((A-N)┬Ęv)/(v┬Ęv) = -2 * ( -[ ... ]/(2d) ) / (v┬Ęv) = [ ... ]/(d v┬Ęv). So t_F = [ d^2(R-r) + d r(R+r) + 2a r d + (R^2 - r^2)(d+r) ]/(d v┬Ęv).

We can simplify the numerator. Let's denote numerator N_F = d^2(R-r) + d r(R+r) + 2a r d + (R^2 - r^2)(d+r). Note that (R^2 - r^2)(d+r) = (R-r)(R+r)(d+r). So N_F = d^2(R-r) + d r(R+r) + 2a r d + (R-r)(R+r)(d+r). Combine terms with (R-r): d^2(R-r) + (R-r)(R+r)(d+r) = (R-r)[ d^2 + (R+r)(d+r) ] = (R-r)[ d^2 + (R+r)d + (R+r)r ] = (R-r)[ d^2 + d(R+r) + r(R+r) ]. Also we have d r(R+r) + 2a r d = d r(R+r) + 2a r d = d r(R+r + 2a). So N_F = (R-r)[ d^2 + d(R+r) + r(R+r) ] + d r(R+r) + 2a r d.

Now note that a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d). So 2a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/d. Then 2a r d = r(d^2+r^2-R^2). So N_F = (R-r)[ d^2 + d(R+r) + r(R+r) ] + d r(R+r) + r(d^2+r^2-R^2). Expand (R-r)[ d^2 + d(R+r) + r(R+r) ] = (R-r)d^2 + (R-r)d(R+r) + (R-r)r(R+r) = (R-r)d^2 + d(R^2-r^2) + r(R^2-r^2). So N_F = (R-r)d^2 + d(R^2-r^2) + r(R^2-r^2) + d r(R+r) + r(d^2+r^2-R^2). Combine the terms: d(R^2-r^2) + d r(R+r) = d[(R^2-r^2) + r(R+r)] = d[ R^2 - r^2 + rR + r^2 ] = d(R^2 + rR) = dR(R+r). Also r(R^2-r^2) + r(d^2+r^2-R^2) = r(R^2-r^2 + d^2+r^2-R^2) = r(d^2) = r d^2. So N_F = (R-r)d^2 + dR(R+r) + r d^2 = d^2(R-r + r) + dR(R+r) = d^2 R + dR(R+r) = dR(d + R + r). So N_F = dR(d+R+r). Nice!

Thus t_F = N_F/(d v┬Ęv) = dR(d+R+r)/(d v┬Ęv) = R(d+R+r)/(v┬Ęv).

So t_F = R(d+R+r)/(v┬Ęv).

Now we have t_E and t_F. Also note that v┬Ęv is positive.

Now we need coordinates of E and F. Compute E = A + t_E v, F = A + t_F v.

We have v_x, v_y. So E = (a + t_E v_x, h + t_E v_y). Similarly, F = (a + t_F v_x, h + t_F v_y).

Given the complexity, perhaps there is a synthetic proof that is more elegant. Let's try to find a synthetic proof.

We have circles ╬® and ╬ō intersecting at A and B. Let M and N be centers. Let C and D be the intersections of line MN with ╬® and ╬ō respectively, with order C-M-N-D. So C is on ╬® on the side of M opposite N, D on ╬ō on the side of N opposite M.

Define P = circumcenter of triangle ACD. So P is the center of circle (ACD). Note that since M is the center of ╬®, MA = MC = r, so M lies on perpendicular bisector of AC. Similarly, N lies on perpendicular bisector of AD. Thus MP is the perpendicular bisector of AC, and NP is the perpendicular bisector of AD. So MP Ō¤é AC and NP Ō¤é AD.

Now line AP meets ╬® again at E and ╬ō again at F. So A, P, E, F are collinear.

Let H be orthocenter of triangle PMN. Since M and N are on line MN, the altitude from P is perpendicular to MN. So PH Ō¤é MN. Also, MH Ō¤é PN and NH Ō¤é PM.

We need to prove that the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to circumcircle of triangle BEF.

Let's try to compute the power of A with respect to circle (BEF). Given the difficulty, perhaps we can use coordinate geometry with a more clever parameterization. Since we have nice expressions for P, A, etc., maybe we can compute the circle (BEF) and the line Ōäō in terms of d, r, R and then show the tangency condition reduces to an identity. Let's attempt to do that with symbolic algebra, using the fact that we have t_E = 1 - (|P|^2 - r^2) and t_F = 1 - (|P-d|^2 - R^2). We can compute these in terms of d, r, R. We already have |P|^2 = rU^2/(2(r-a)) with U = d+R-r. And we have r-a = (R^2 - (d-r)^2)/(2d) = ((R-d+r)(R+d-r))/(2d). So |P|^2 = rU^2/(2) * (2d)/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) = r d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)). So |P|^2 = r d (d+R-r)^2 / ((R-d+r)(R+d-r)). Then |P|^2 - r^2 = r d (d+R-r)^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) - r^2. That is messy.

But maybe we can find simpler expressions for t_E and t_F using the fact that P is circumcenter of ACD. There might be a relation: The power of P with respect to ╬® is PC^2 - r^2? Actually, P is on perpendicular bisector of AC, so PA = PC. So PC^2 = PA^2. So power of P with respect to ╬® is PA^2 - r^2. That is the same as |P|^2 - r^2? Wait, M is at origin, so |P|^2 = PA^2? Not exactly: PA is distance from P to A, but |P| is distance from P to M. So |P|^2 = PM^2. So power of P with respect to ╬® is PM^2 - r^2. That is not PA^2 - r^2 unless PM = PA. But we have PA = PC = PD, but not necessarily equal to PM. So power_P(╬®) = PM^2 - r^2. And we have t_E = 1 - (PM^2 - r^2). So that's fine.

Similarly, power_P(╬ō) = PN^2 - R^2, and t_F = 1 - (PN^2 - R^2).

Now we can compute PM^2 and PN^2 using coordinates. We have M=(0,0), N=(d,0), P=(p_x,p_y). So PM^2 = p_x^2+p_y^2, PN^2 = (p_x-d)^2+p_y^2. And we have expressions for p_x and p_y in terms of a, h, r, d, R. But we also have a and h expressed in terms of d, r, R. So we can compute PM^2 - r^2 and PN^2 - R^2. Let's do that.

We have:

a = (d^2 + r^2 - R^2)/(2d)
h^2 = r^2 - a^2

p_x = (d+R-r)/2
p_y = - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h)

Actually (R-d+r) = R - d + r, and (R+d-r) = R + d - r. So PM^2 = r d U^2 / ((R-d+r)(R+d-r)). Then PM^2 - r^2 = r d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) - r^2 = r [ d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) - r ].

Now t_E = 1 - (PM^2 - r^2) = 1 - r [ d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) - r ] = 1 - r d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) + r^2.

Similarly, PN^2 = (p_x-d)^2 + p_y^2. p_x-d = (d+R-r)/2 - d = (R-r-d)/2 = -(d+R-r? Actually R-r-d = -(d - R + r) = -V? Where V = d-R+r. So p_x-d = -V/2. So (p_x-d)^2 = V^2/4. p_y^2 = (r+a)^2 U^2/(4h^2) = (r+a)^2 U^2/(4(r^2-a^2)) = (r+a)^2 U^2/(4(r-a)(r+a)) = (r+a)U^2/(4(r-a)). So PN^2 = V^2/4 + (r+a)U^2/(4(r-a)) = (1/4)[V^2 + (r+a)U^2/(r-a)]. Then PN^2 - R^2 = (1/4)[V^2 + (r+a)U^2/(r-a)] - R^2. And t_F = 1 - (PN^2 - R^2) = 1 - (1/4)[V^2 + (r+a)U^2/(r-a)] + R^2 = 1 + R^2 - (1/4)[V^2 + (r+a)U^2/(r-a)].

Now we also have expressions for a, h, etc. Perhaps we can find that t_E and t_F are related to the coordinates of H. H = (p_x, y_H) with y_H = - h (d-R+r)/(2(r+a)) = - h V/(2(r+a)). So y_H = - h V/(2(r+a)). Also, note that V = d-R+r. And U = d+R-r.

But we also have p_y - h = - (r+a)U/(2h) - h = - (r+a)U/(2h) - h. That's consistent.

Now we can compute E and F coordinates in terms of A and v. But maybe we can find that the circle (BEF) has its center on the line through the midpoint of AB? Actually, B is (a, -h). Given the difficulty, maybe we can use coordinate geometry but with a more systematic approach: Compute the circle (BEF) equation in terms of A and P, and then compute the condition for tangency of line through H parallel to AP. Since we have t_E = 1 - (PM^2 - r^2) and t_F = 1 - (PN^2 - R^2), we can express E and F as:

E = A + (1 - (PM^2 - r^2)) (P-A) = (1 - (PM^2 - r^2)) P + (PM^2 - r^2) A? Actually, E = A + t_E (P-A) = (1-t_E)A + t_E P. So E = (1-t_E)A + t_E P. Similarly, F = (1-t_F)A + t_F P.

Now B = reflection of A across x-axis: B = (a, -h). In complex numbers, if we set M=0, N=d real, then A = a+ih, B = a-ih.

Now we can compute the circumcircle of B, E, F. Since E and F are linear combinations of A and P, and B is symmetric of A, maybe we can find that the circle (BEF) is the image of the circle through A, E, F under reflection? But A, E, F collinear, so degenerate.

Alternatively, consider the circle through B, E, F. Its center O can be found as the intersection of perpendicular bisectors. Since E and F lie on line AP, the perpendicular bisector of EF is the line perpendicular to AP through the midpoint of EF. That line is also the perpendicular bisector of EF. The perpendicular bisector of BE is some line. The intersection gives O. Maybe we can compute O in terms of A, P, B.

Let's attempt to compute O using vector geometry. LetŌĆÖs denote the line AP. LetŌĆÖs set up a coordinate system where the x-axis is MN, and y-axis is perpendicular. We already have that. But maybe we can use complex numbers with M=0, N=d real. Then A = a+ih, B = a-ih. P = p_x+ip_y with p_y negative. We have v = P-A = (p_x-a) + i(p_y-h). We have t_E = 1 - (|P|^2 - r^2) = 1 - (p_x^2+p_y^2 - r^2). And t_F = 1 - (|P-d|^2 - R^2) = 1 - ((p_x-d)^2+p_y^2 - R^2). So E = (1-t_E)A + t_E P, F = (1-t_F)A + t_F P.

Now we need to show that the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to circle (BEF). Since H is orthocenter of triangle PMN, we can compute H in complex numbers. For triangle with vertices M=0, N=d real, P = p_x+ip_y. The orthocenter H is given by: H = M + N + P - (circumcenter? Actually, for triangle with vertices z1,z2,z3, the orthocenter is z1+z2+z3 - 2*circumcenter. But we can also compute directly: Since M and N are on real axis, the altitude from P is vertical line x = p_x. The altitude from M is line through M perpendicular to PN. So H = (p_x, y_H) with y_H = (p_x(d-p_x))/p_y? Actually, we derived y_H = p_x(d-p_x)/p_y. So H = p_x + i * (p_x(d-p_x)/p_y). So H = p_x + i * (p_x(d-p_x)/p_y). That is a complex number.

Maybe we can compute the equation of the circle (BEF) in the form: |X|^2 + u x + v y + w = 0. Then the condition that line Ōäō is tangent is that the equation for s has discriminant zero. For tangency, discriminant = 0: (2 (v┬ĘH + u v_x + v v_y))^2 - 4 |v|^2 (|H|^2 + u H_x + v H_y + w) = 0 => (v┬ĘH + u v_x + v v_y)^2 = |v|^2 (|H|^2 + u H_x + v H_y + w). LetŌĆÖs denote complex numbers: A = a+ih, B = a-ih, P = p_x+ip_y. Then v = P-A = (p_x-a)+i(p_y-h). We have t_E = 1 - (|P|^2 - r^2). Note that |P|^2 = P * conjugate(P). And r^2 = |A|^2 = A * conjugate(A). So |P|^2 - r^2 = P*conj(P) - A*conj(A). That is a real number. Similarly, t_F = 1 - (|P-d|^2 - R^2) = 1 - ((P-d)*conj(P-d) - R^2). Since R^2 = |A-d|^2 = (A-d)*conj(A-d). So t_F = 1 - (|P-d|^2 - |A-d|^2). So t_F = 1 - ( (P-d)(conj(P)-d) - (A-d)(conj(A)-d) ) = 1 - ( P conj(P) - d(P+conj(P)) + d^2 - (A conj(A) - d(A+conj(A)) + d^2 ) = 1 - ( |P|^2 - |A|^2 - d(P+conj(P) - A - conj(A)) ). So t_F = 1 - ( (|P|^2 - |A|^2) - d( (P+conj(P)) - (A+conj(A)) ) ). But |P|^2 - |A|^2 = (P conj(P) - A conj(A)). And P+conj(P) = 2 Re(P), A+conj(A)=2 Re(A). So t_F = 1 - ( (|P|^2 - |A|^2) - 2d(Re(P)-Re(A)) = 1 - (|P|^2 - |A|^2) + 2d(Re(P)-Re(A)). That is t_F = 1 - (|P|^2 - |A|^2) + 2d(Re(P)-Re(A)). But we also have t_E = 1 - (|P|^2 - |A|^2) because |A|^2 = r^2. So t_E = 1 - (|P|^2 - |A|^2). So t_F = t_E + 2d(Re(P)-Re(A)). That is interesting.

Now Re(P)-Re(A) = p_x - a. And we computed p_x - a = (R-r)U/(2d). So t_F = t_E + 2d * ((R-r)U/(2d)) = t_E + (R-r)U. So t_F = t_E + (R-r)U. Since U = d+R-r. So t_F = t_E + (R-r)(d+R-r). That is a relation.

Now we can also compute t_E explicitly: t_E = 1 - (|P|^2 - |A|^2). We have |P|^2 = r d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)). And |A|^2 = r^2. So t_E = 1 - r d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) + r^2. That's not simple.

Now we can compute P = circumcenter of triangle ACD. Points: A=(0,a), C=(p-r,0), D=(q+R,0). So C and D are on x-axis. So the perpendicular bisector of CD is vertical line through the midpoint of CD: midpoint = ((p-r)+(q+R))/2 = (p+q+R-r)/2. So P lies on that vertical line: x = (p+q+R-r)/2. Also, P is equidistant from A and C. So we can compute P = (x_P, y_P) with x_P = (p+q+R-r)/2. Then we can find y_P from PA^2 = PC^2.

We have PA^2 = (x_P-0)^2 + (y_P-a)^2 = x_P^2 + (y_P-a)^2.
PC^2 = (x_P - (p-r))^2 + (y_P-0)^2 = (x_P - p + r)^2 + y_P^2.
Set equal: x_P^2 + (y_P-a)^2 = (x_P - p + r)^2 + y_P^2.
Expand: x_P^2 + y_P^2 -2a y_P + a^2 = (x_P - p + r)^2 + y_P^2 = x_P^2 + (p-r)^2 -2x_P(p-r) + y_P^2.
Cancel x_P^2 and y_P^2: -2a y_P + a^2 = (p-r)^2 -2x_P(p-r).
Thus 2a y_P = a^2 - (p-r)^2 + 2x_P(p-r).
So y_P = [a^2 - (p-r)^2 + 2x_P(p-r)]/(2a).

Now we can substitute x_P = (p+q+R-r)/2. Also, note that r^2 = p^2+a^2, R^2 = q^2+a^2. So we can simplify.

So H = (x_P, y_H) where y_H is such that HM Ō¤é PN. Compute PN: N=(q,0), P=(x_P, y_P). So vector PN = (q - x_P, -y_P). The line through M=(p,0) perpendicular to PN has direction vector (y_P, q - x_P) (since dot: (q-x_P, -y_P)┬Ę(y_P, q-x_P)= (q-x_P)y_P + (-y_P)(q-x_P)=0). So equation: (x,y) = (p,0) + t(y_P, q-x_P). Intersection with x=x_P gives: x_P = p + t y_P => t = (x_P - p)/y_P. Then y_H = 0 + t (q-x_P) = (x_P - p)(q-x_P)/y_P. So H = (x_P, (x_P-p)(q-x_P)/y_P). That is the orthocenter.

Maybe we can find a nicer expression for y_P. Let's compute directly using coordinates.

We can compute these using the relations. Maybe we can find a simpler expression for ╬╗_E and ╬╗_F. Note that |P-M|^2 - r^2 = (x_P-p)^2 + y_P^2 - r^2. And we have r^2 = p^2+a^2. So |P-M|^2 - r^2 = (x_P-p)^2 + y_P^2 - p^2 - a^2.

These equalities give relations that might simplify the expressions for ╬╗_E and ╬╗_F.

Now, we can compute |P-M|^2 - r^2 in terms of |v|^2 and other known. Since M is at (p,0), we have:

|P-M|^2 = (x_P-p)^2 + y_P^2.
But we also have |P-A|^2 = x_P^2 + (y_P-a)^2.
We can express (x_P-p)^2 = (x_P^2 -2p x_P + p^2). So |P-M|^2 = x_P^2 -2p x_P + p^2 + y_P^2.
Thus |P-M|^2 - r^2 = x_P^2 -2p x_P + p^2 + y_P^2 - (p^2+a^2) = x_P^2 -2p x_P + y_P^2 - a^2.
So |P-M|^2 - r^2 = (x_P^2 + y_P^2 - a^2) - 2p x_P.

Now, |v|^2 = x_P^2 + (y_P-a)^2 = x_P^2 + y_P^2 -2a y_P + a^2.
So x_P^2 + y_P^2 = |v|^2 + 2a y_P - a^2.
Thus |P-M|^2 - r^2 = (|v|^2 + 2a y_P - a^2) - a^2 - 2p x_P = |v|^2 + 2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2p x_P.
So ╬╗_E = 1 - (|P-M|^2 - r^2)/|v|^2 = 1 - (|v|^2 + 2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2p x_P)/|v|^2 = 1 - 1 - (2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2p x_P)/|v|^2 = - (2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2p x_P)/|v|^2 = (2a^2 + 2p x_P - 2a y_P)/|v|^2 = 2(a^2 + p x_P - a y_P)/|v|^2.

So ╬╗_E = 2(a^2 + p x_P - a y_P)/|v|^2.

Similarly, we can compute ╬╗_F = 1 - (|P-N|^2 - R^2)/|v|^2. Compute |P-N|^2 = (x_P-q)^2 + y_P^2 = x_P^2 -2q x_P + q^2 + y_P^2. Then |P-N|^2 - R^2 = x_P^2 -2q x_P + q^2 + y_P^2 - (q^2+a^2) = x_P^2 + y_P^2 - a^2 - 2q x_P. Then using x_P^2+y_P^2 = |v|^2 + 2a y_P - a^2, we get |P-N|^2 - R^2 = |v|^2 + 2a y_P - a^2 - a^2 - 2q x_P = |v|^2 + 2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2q x_P. Then ╬╗_F = 1 - (|v|^2 + 2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2q x_P)/|v|^2 = - (2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2q x_P)/|v|^2 = 2(a^2 + q x_P - a y_P)/|v|^2.

Thus we have:

╬╗_E = 2(a^2 + p x_P - a y_P)/|v|^2
╬╗_F = 2(a^2 + q x_P - a y_P)/|v|^2

Now we also have expressions for x_P and y_P in terms of p, q, a, r, R. But we can also express a^2 + p x_P - a y_P and a^2 + q x_P - a y_P in terms of known.

Recall x_P = (p+q+R-r)/2, y_P = [a^2 + (p-r)(q+R)]/(2a). So compute a^2 + p x_P - a y_P = a^2 + p*(p+q+R-r)/2 - a * ([a^2 + (p-r)(q+R)]/(2a)) = a^2 + p(p+q+R-r)/2 - (a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))/2 = a^2 + (p(p+q+R-r) - a^2 - (p-r)(q+R))/2 = a^2 + (p(p+q+R-r) - a^2 - (p-r)(q+R))/2.

Simplify inside: p(p+q+R-r) - (p-r)(q+R) = p^2 + pq + pR - pr - (p(q+R) - r(q+R)) = p^2 + pq + pR - pr - pq - pR + r(q+R) = p^2 - pr + r(q+R) = p(p-r) + r(q+R) = p(p-r) + r(q+R). So then numerator = p(p-r) + r(q+R) - a^2. So a^2 + (p(p-r) + r(q+R) - a^2)/2 = a^2 + (p(p-r) + r(q+R) - a^2)/2 = (2a^2 + p(p-r) + r(q+R) - a^2)/2 = (a^2 + p(p-r) + r(q+R))/2.

Thus a^2 + p x_P - a y_P = (a^2 + p(p-r) + r(q+R))/2.

Similarly, a^2 + q x_P - a y_P = a^2 + q*(p+q+R-r)/2 - (a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))/2 = a^2 + (q(p+q+R-r) - a^2 - (p-r)(q+R))/2 = (2a^2 + q(p+q+R-r) - a^2 - (p-r)(q+R))/2 = (a^2 + q(p+q+R-r) - (p-r)(q+R))/2.

Compute q(p+q+R-r) - (p-r)(q+R) = qp + q^2 + qR - qr - (p(q+R) - r(q+R)) = pq + q^2 + qR - qr - pq - pR + r(q+R) = q^2 + qR - qr - pR + rq + rR = q^2 + qR - pR + rR = q^2 + R(q - p + r) = q^2 + R(d + r) where d = q-p. So then a^2 + q x_P - a y_P = (a^2 + q^2 + R(d+r))/2.

But we can also use the relation R^2 = q^2+a^2. So q^2 = R^2 - a^2. Then a^2 + q^2 + R(d+r) = a^2 + (R^2 - a^2) + R(d+r) = R^2 + R(d+r) = R(R + d + r) = R(R + d + r). So a^2 + q x_P - a y_P = R(R + d + r)/2.

Similarly, for the other expression: a^2 + p x_P - a y_P = (a^2 + p(p-r) + r(q+R))/2. We can also express p(p-r) = p^2 - pr. And r(q+R) = rq + rR. So a^2 + p^2 - pr + rq + rR = (p^2+a^2) - pr + rq + rR = r^2 - pr + rq + rR = r(r - p + q + R) = r(r + q + R - p). So a^2 + p x_P - a y_P = r(r + q + R - p)/2 = r(r + q + R - p)/2. But note that r + q + R - p = (q-p) + (r+R) = d + r + R. So that is r(d+r+R)/2. So a^2 + p x_P - a y_P = r(d+r+R)/2.

Thus we have:

╬╗_E = 2 * (r(d+r+R)/2) / |v|^2 = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2.
╬╗_F = 2 * (R(R+d+r)/2) / |v|^2 = R(R+d+r)/|v|^2.

So ╬╗_E = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2, ╬╗_F = R(R+d+r)/|v|^2.

The radius is distance from O to B: sqrt((0.6026)^2 + (-0.8976+0.7599)^2) = sqrt(0.3631 + (-0.1377)^2)= sqrt(0.3631+0.0189)= sqrt(0.382)=0.618. Now H = (x_P, y_H) = (1.1, y_H). Compute y_H = a(d^2 - (R-r)^2)/[2(a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))]? Actually we derived y_H = a(d^2 - (R-r)^2)/[2(a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))]. Compute a^2 + (p-r)(q+R) = 0.5775 + (-0.65-1)*(1.85+2)=0.5775 + (-1.65)*(3.85)=0.5775-6.3725=-5.795. So denominator = 2*(-5.795)= -11.59. d^2=6.25, (R-r)^2=1, so d^2-(R-r)^2=5.25. Then y_H = a*5.25/(-11.59)=0.7599*5.25/(-11.59)=3.989/(-11.59)= -0.344. So H = (1.1, -0.344). The line Ōäō through H parallel to v: v=(1.1,-4.5769). So Ōäō: (x,y) = (1.1, -0.344) + s(1.1, -4.5769). Now compute distance from O=(0.6026,-0.8976) to Ōäō. Vector from H to O: (0.6026-1.1, -0.8976+0.344)= (-0.4974, -0.5536). Cross product with v: (-0.4974)*(-4.5769) - (-0.5536)*(1.1) = 2.277 + 0.6089 = 2.8859. |v| = sqrt(1.21+20.94)= sqrt(22.15)=4.706. So distance = 2.8859/4.706 = 0.613. That is approximately equal to radius 0.618. So the line is tangent! The slight discrepancy is due to rounding. So the tangency condition holds.

Thus we have a promising analytic approach: We have derived expressions for ╬╗_E, ╬╗_F, and H in terms of p, q, a, r, R, d. Now we need to prove that the line through H parallel to v is tangent to circle (BEF). This is a condition that can be expressed as: The distance from the circumcenter O of triangle BEF to line Ōäō equals the radius of that circle. We can compute O and radius using coordinates. Since we have nice expressions, maybe we can find that O lies on the line through the midpoint of AB? Actually, in our numeric, O=(0.6026,-0.8976) and midpoint of AB is (0,0). So O is not on the y-axis. But maybe O is the midpoint of something like the segment connecting the projections of H onto the lines through P? Not.

Given that we have analytic expressions, we can compute O directly using the fact that B, E, F are points. Since we have expressions for E and F in terms of A and P, and B is symmetric of A, we can compute the circumcenter O using vector formulas. Let's attempt to do that with general parameters.

We have:

A = (0, a)
B = (0, -a)
P = (x_P, y_P)
v = P - A = (x_P, y_P - a)

We have ╬╗_E = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2, ╬╗_F = R(R+d+r)/|v|^2.

Thus:

E = A + ╬╗_E v = (1-╬╗_E)A + ╬╗_E P
F = A + ╬╗_F v = (1-╬╗_F)A + ╬╗_F P

Now, we can compute the circumcenter O of triangle BEF. Since B is symmetric of A across x-axis, and E and F are on line AP, there might be a relation that O is the image of some point under reflection. Perhaps we can find that O is the midpoint of the segment connecting the projections of H onto the lines through P? Not.

There is a known formula: For a line L through A, the circle through B and the two intersections of L with circles ╬® and ╬ō is the circle with diameter the midpoint of something? Actually, the polar of a point X with respect to a circle is the line through the points of tangency of the two tangents from X. Given the analytic success, we can attempt to compute O and radius in terms of p, q, a, and then verify the tangency condition algebraically. This is a computational problem, but with careful algebraic manipulation, it might be doable. Since we have derived ╬╗_E and ╬╗_F, and we have expressions for x_P and y_P in terms of p, q, a, r, R, and we also have r^2 = p^2+a^2, R^2 = q^2+a^2, and d = q-p. We can also express r and R in terms of p and a, etc. So we can treat p, q, a as independent parameters with the condition that p<q and a>0, and r = sqrt(p^2+a^2), R = sqrt(q^2+a^2). Then we can compute everything in terms of p, q, a. This is a bit messy but we can try to simplify using the fact that many expressions involve r and R, and we can also use the relations between them.

Let's define:

LetŌĆÖs denote:

x_P = (p+q+R-r)/2
y_P = (a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))/(2a)

We have v = (x_P, y_P-a). So |v|^2 = x_P^2 + (y_P-a)^2.

We also have ╬╗_E = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2, ╬╗_F = R(R+d+r)/|v|^2.

Now, we need to compute the circumcenter O of triangle BEF. Since B=(0,-a), E and F are on line AP. Perhaps we can find O by using the fact that the perpendicular bisector of EF is the line through the midpoint of EF perpendicular to v. That line is also the perpendicular bisector of EF. And the perpendicular bisector of BE is some line. Their intersection gives O.

LetŌĆÖs compute the midpoint of EF. Since E = A + ╬╗_E v, F = A + ╬╗_F v, the midpoint M_EF = A + (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)/2 v. So M_EF = (0,a) + ((╬╗_E+╬╗_F)/2) (x_P, y_P-a). So M_EF = ( ((╬╗_E+╬╗_F)/2) x_P, a + ((╬╗_E+╬╗_F)/2)(y_P-a) ).

The perpendicular bisector of EF is the line through M_EF with direction perpendicular to v. So its equation: (X - M_EF) ┬Ę v = 0, i.e., v ┬Ę (X - M_EF) = 0.

Now, the perpendicular bisector of BE: B=(0,-a), E=(E_x, E_y). The midpoint of BE is M_BE = (E_x/2, (E_y - a)/2). The direction of BE is (E_x, E_y + a). So the perpendicular bisector is the line through M_BE with direction perpendicular to BE. Its equation: (X - M_BE) ┬Ę (E_x, E_y + a) = 0.

The intersection O satisfies both. So we can solve for O.

But maybe we can find a simpler expression for O. Since B is symmetric of A across x-axis, and E and F are on AP, the circle (BEF) might be symmetric to the circle through A and the reflections of E and F? Not.

Another approach: Use complex numbers. LetŌĆÖs set up complex coordinates with the midpoint of AB as origin, and the line of centers as real axis. So A = i a, B = -i a, M = p (real), N = q (real), with p<q. Then we have:

P = (p+q+R-r)/2 + i * (a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))/(2a) = x_P + i y_P.
v = P - A = x_P + i(y_P - a).

We have ╬╗_E = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2, ╬╗_F = R(R+d+r)/|v|^2, where d = q-p.

Then E = A + ╬╗_E v = i a + ╬╗_E (x_P + i(y_P-a)) = ╬╗_E x_P + i (a + ╬╗_E (y_P-a)).
Similarly, F = ╬╗_F x_P + i (a + ╬╗_F (y_P-a)).

Now, B = -i a.

We need to show that the line through H parallel to v is tangent to circle (BEF). H = (x_P, y_H) with y_H = a(d^2 - (R-r)^2)/[2(a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))]? So that's fine.

Now, the line Ōäō: X = H + s v = x_P + i y_H + s (x_P + i(y_P-a)) = (1+s)x_P + i (y_H + s(y_P-a)).

We need to show that Ōäō is tangent to circle through B, E, F. This is a condition that can be expressed as: The power of H with respect to that circle equals the square of the distance from H to the point of tangency along Ōäō, but we can also compute the distance from the center O to Ōäō equals radius.

Given the complexity, perhaps we can use the fact that the line through H parallel to AP is the radical axis of two circles that are tangent to each other? Given the analytic success, we can try to compute O and radius in terms of p, q, a, and then verify the tangency condition algebraically. This is a heavy but straightforward computation. Since we have expressions for ╬╗_E and ╬╗_F, we can compute the circumcenter O using the formula for the circumcenter of three points in complex numbers. For points z1, z2, z3, the circumcenter is given by:

O = (|z1|^2 (z2 - z3) + |z2|^2 (z3 - z1) + |z3|^2 (z1 - z2)) / (z1 (z2 - z3) + z2 (z3 - z1) + z3 (z1 - z2))? Actually, that formula gives the circumcenter if the points are not collinear. But that's messy.

Alternatively, we can compute O as the intersection of perpendicular bisectors. Since we have coordinates, we can compute O by solving linear equations. Let's do that with general parameters.

LetŌĆÖs denote:

B = (0, -a)
E = (E_x, E_y) = (╬╗_E x_P, a + ╬╗_E (y_P - a)) = (╬╗_E x_P, a + ╬╗_E y_P - ╬╗_E a) = (╬╗_E x_P, a(1-╬╗_E) + ╬╗_E y_P)
Similarly, F = (╬╗_F x_P, a(1-╬╗_F) + ╬╗_F y_P)

Now, we can compute the perpendicular bisector of BE. The midpoint M_BE = (E_x/2, (E_y - a)/2) = (╬╗_E x_P/2, (a(1-╬╗_E) + ╬╗_E y_P - a)/2) = (╬╗_E x_P/2, (-a ╬╗_E + ╬╗_E y_P)/2) = (╬╗_E x_P/2, ╬╗_E (y_P - a)/2). So M_BE = (╬╗_E x_P/2, ╬╗_E (y_P - a)/2).

The vector BE = (E_x - 0, E_y - (-a)) = (╬╗_E x_P, a(1-╬╗_E) + ╬╗_E y_P + a) = (╬╗_E x_P, a(1-╬╗_E+1) + ╬╗_E y_P) = (╬╗_E x_P, a(2-╬╗_E) + ╬╗_E y_P). But note that E_y + a = a(1-╬╗_E) + ╬╗_E y_P + a = a(2-╬╗_E) + ╬╗_E y_P.

So the perpendicular bisector of BE is the line through M_BE with direction perpendicular to BE. Its equation: (X - M_BE) ┬Ę (E_x, E_y + a) = 0. So:

(X_x - ╬╗_E x_P/2) * (╬╗_E x_P) + (X_y - ╬╗_E (y_P - a)/2) * (a(2-╬╗_E) + ╬╗_E y_P) = 0.

Similarly, the perpendicular bisector of EF: M_EF = ( (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)x_P/2, a + (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)(y_P - a)/2 ) = ( (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)x_P/2, a + (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)(y_P - a)/2 ). The vector EF = ( (╬╗_F-╬╗_E)x_P, (╬╗_F-╬╗_E)(y_P - a) ) = (╬╗_F-╬╗_E) v. So the perpendicular bisector of EF is the line through M_EF with direction perpendicular to v. Its equation: (X - M_EF) ┬Ę v = 0, i.e.,:

(X_x - (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)x_P/2) * x_P + (X_y - a - (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)(y_P - a)/2) * (y_P - a) = 0.

Now, we need to find O = (X_x, X_y) that satisfies both. This is a system of two linear equations in X_x and X_y. We can solve for X_x and X_y.

LetŌĆÖs denote:

v_x = x_P, v_y = y_P - a.

Then we have:

Equation (1): (X_x - ╬╗_E x_P/2) * (╬╗_E x_P) + (X_y - ╬╗_E v_y/2) * (a(2-╬╗_E) + ╬╗_E y_P) = 0.
Equation (2): (X_x - (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)x_P/2) * x_P + (X_y - a - (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)v_y/2) * v_y = 0.

We can simplify these. Note that a(2-╬╗_E) + ╬╗_E y_P = 2a - a ╬╗_E + ╬╗_E y_P = 2a + ╬╗_E (y_P - a) = 2a + ╬╗_E v_y.

So equation (1) becomes:

╬╗_E x_P (X_x - ╬╗_E x_P/2) + (2a + ╬╗_E v_y)(X_y - ╬╗_E v_y/2) = 0.

Expand: ╬╗_E x_P X_x - ╬╗_E^2 x_P^2/2 + (2a + ╬╗_E v_y) X_y - (2a + ╬╗_E v_y) ╬╗_E v_y/2 = 0.

Thus:

╬╗_E x_P X_x + (2a + ╬╗_E v_y) X_y = ╬╗_E^2 x_P^2/2 + (2a + ╬╗_E v_y) ╬╗_E v_y/2 = (╬╗_E/2)[ ╬╗_E x_P^2 + (2a + ╬╗_E v_y) v_y ] = (╬╗_E/2)[ ╬╗_E x_P^2 + 2a v_y + ╬╗_E v_y^2 ] = (╬╗_E/2)[ ╬╗_E (x_P^2+v_y^2) + 2a v_y ].

But note that |v|^2 = x_P^2 + v_y^2. So ╬╗_E (x_P^2+v_y^2) = ╬╗_E |v|^2. And we have ╬╗_E = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2. So ╬╗_E |v|^2 = r(d+r+R). So ╬╗_E (x_P^2+v_y^2) = r(d+r+R). Thus the right side becomes (╬╗_E/2)[ r(d+r+R) + 2a v_y ].

So equation (1): ╬╗_E x_P X_x + (2a + ╬╗_E v_y) X_y = (╬╗_E/2)[ r(d+r+R) + 2a v_y ].   (1)

Now equation (2): x_P (X_x - (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)x_P/2) + v_y (X_y - a - (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)v_y/2) = 0.

Expand: x_P X_x - (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)x_P^2/2 + v_y X_y - v_y a - (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)v_y^2/2 = 0.

Thus:

x_P X_x + v_y X_y = (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)x_P^2/2 + a v_y + (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)v_y^2/2 = (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)(x_P^2+v_y^2)/2 + a v_y = (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)|v|^2/2 + a v_y.

Now we have ╬╗_E+╬╗_F = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2 + R(R+d+r)/|v|^2 = (r(d+r+R) + R(R+d+r))/|v|^2 = (r d + r^2 + r R + R^2 + R d + R r)/|v|^2 = (r d + R d + r^2 + R^2 + 2rR)/|v|^2 = (d(r+R) + (r^2+2rR+R^2))/|v|^2 = (d(r+R) + (r+R)^2)/|v|^2 = (r+R)(d+r+R)/|v|^2.

So ╬╗_E+╬╗_F = (r+R)(d+r+R)/|v|^2.

Thus (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)|v|^2 = (r+R)(d+r+R). So the right side of equation (2) becomes (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y.

So equation (2): x_P X_x + v_y X_y = (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y.   (2)

Now we have two linear equations in X_x and X_y. We can solve for X_x and X_y. LetŌĆÖs denote:

Equation (1): ╬╗_E x_P X_x + (2a + ╬╗_E v_y) X_y = (╬╗_E/2)[ r(d+r+R) + 2a v_y ].
Equation (2): x_P X_x + v_y X_y = (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y.

We can solve this system. LetŌĆÖs write them as:

A1 X_x + B1 X_y = C1
A2 X_x + B2 X_y = C2

with:

A1 = ╬╗_E x_P
B1 = 2a + ╬╗_E v_y
C1 = (╬╗_E/2)[ r(d+r+R) + 2a v_y ]

A2 = x_P
B2 = v_y
C2 = (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y

Now, we can solve for X_x and X_y using determinants. The solution:

X_x = (C1 B2 - C2 B1) / (A1 B2 - A2 B1)
X_y = (A1 C2 - A2 C1) / (A1 B2 - A2 B1)

We need to compute these expressions. This is messy, but we can try to simplify using the relations.

First, compute the denominator D = A1 B2 - A2 B1 = ╬╗_E x_P * v_y - x_P * (2a + ╬╗_E v_y) = x_P (╬╗_E v_y - 2a - ╬╗_E v_y) = x_P (-2a) = -2a x_P.

So D = -2a x_P. That's nice!

Thus D = -2a x_P.

Now compute numerator for X_x: N_x = C1 B2 - C2 B1 = C1 v_y - C2 (2a + ╬╗_E v_y) = v_y C1 - 2a C2 - ╬╗_E v_y C2 = v_y (C1 - ╬╗_E C2) - 2a C2.

So X_x = N_x / D = [v_y (C1 - ╬╗_E C2) - 2a C2] / (-2a x_P) = - [v_y (C1 - ╬╗_E C2) - 2a C2] / (2a x_P) = [ -v_y (C1 - ╬╗_E C2) + 2a C2 ] / (2a x_P) = [ 2a C2 - v_y (C1 - ╬╗_E C2) ] / (2a x_P).

Now compute C1 and C2.

C1 = (╬╗_E/2)[ r(d+r+R) + 2a v_y ].
C2 = (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y.

Now compute C1 - ╬╗_E C2 = (╬╗_E/2)[ r(d+r+R) + 2a v_y ] - ╬╗_E [ (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y ] = ╬╗_E [ (1/2)(r(d+r+R) + 2a v_y) - (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) - a v_y ] = ╬╗_E [ (1/2)(r(d+r+R) - (r+R)(d+r+R)) + (1/2)(2a v_y) - a v_y ] = ╬╗_E [ (1/2)( (r - (r+R))(d+r+R) ) + a v_y - a v_y ] = ╬╗_E [ (1/2)( -R (d+r+R) ) + 0 ] = - (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/2.

Thus C1 - ╬╗_E C2 = - (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/2.

Now plug into N_x: v_y (C1 - ╬╗_E C2) - 2a C2 = v_y * ( - (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/2 ) - 2a C2 = - (╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R))/2 - 2a C2.

So X_x = [ 2a C2 - ( - (╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R))/2 )? Wait, we have X_x = [ 2a C2 - v_y (C1 - ╬╗_E C2) ] / (2a x_P). Since we had X_x = [2a C2 - v_y (C1 - ╬╗_E C2)]/(2a x_P). So plug: 2a C2 - v_y (C1 - ╬╗_E C2) = 2a C2 - v_y * ( - (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/2 ) = 2a C2 + (╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R))/2.

Thus X_x = [ 2a C2 + (╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R))/2 ] / (2a x_P) = [ 2a C2 ]/(2a x_P) + [ (╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R))/2 ]/(2a x_P) = C2/x_P + (╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R))/(4a x_P).

Now C2 = (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y. So C2/x_P = [ (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y ] / x_P.

Thus X_x = [ (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y ] / x_P + (╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R))/(4a x_P).

Now we also have ╬╗_E = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2. And v_y = y_P - a. But we might want to express everything in terms of p, q, a, r, R, d. However, note that x_P = (p+q+R-r)/2. Also, v_y = y_P - a. We have y_P = [a^2 + (p-r)(q+R)]/(2a). So v_y = [a^2 + (p-r)(q+R)]/(2a) - a = [a^2 + (p-r)(q+R) - 2a^2]/(2a) = [ (p-r)(q+R) - a^2 ]/(2a). So v_y = [ (p-r)(q+R) - a^2 ]/(2a).

We also have r^2 = p^2+a^2, R^2 = q^2+a^2. And d = q-p.

Now, we also need X_y. Let's compute X_y similarly.

X_y = (A1 C2 - A2 C1) / D = (╬╗_E x_P C2 - x_P C1) / (-2a x_P) = (╬╗_E C2 - C1) / (-2a) = (C1 - ╬╗_E C2) / (2a).

We already computed C1 - ╬╗_E C2 = - (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/2. So X_y = [ - (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/2 ] / (2a) = - (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/(4a).

Thus X_y = - (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/(4a).

Now we have O = (X_x, X_y). Note that X_y is expressed in terms of ╬╗_E, R, d, r, R. But ╬╗_E = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2. So X_y = - (r(d+r+R) * R (d+r+R))/(4a |v|^2) = - (r R (d+r+R)^2)/(4a |v|^2).

Now we also have X_x. Let's simplify X_x.

X_x = C2/x_P + (╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R))/(4a x_P). Since we have ╬╗_E = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2, then ╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R)/(4a x_P) = r(d+r+R) * R * v_y * (d+r+R) / (4a x_P |v|^2) = r R v_y (d+r+R)^2/(4a x_P |v|^2).

Now C2 = (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y. So C2/x_P = [ (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y ] / x_P.

Thus X_x = [ (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y ] / x_P + r R v_y (d+r+R)^2/(4a x_P |v|^2).

Now we need to compute the radius squared of circle (BEF). Since O is the circumcenter, radius^2 = |O - B|^2 = (X_x - 0)^2 + (X_y + a)^2 = X_x^2 + (X_y + a)^2.

We also need to compute the distance from O to line Ōäō. Line Ōäō: X = H + s v, with H = (x_P, y_H). So the distance from O to Ōäō is |(O - H) ├Ś v| / |v|. We need to show that this distance equals radius.

Thus we need to show: |(O - H) ├Ś v| = |v| * radius.

Now, O - H = (X_x - x_P, X_y - y_H). The cross product with v: (X_x - x_P)*v_y - (X_y - y_H)*v_x. So we need to compute this and compare with |v| * sqrt(X_x^2 + (X_y+a)^2). This is a heavy algebraic condition.

Let's proceed with the analytic proof.

We have:

Parameters: p, q, a (real numbers with a>0, p<q). Define:
r = sqrt(p^2+a^2)
R = sqrt(q^2+a^2)
d = q-p

We have:
x_P = (p+q+R-r)/2
y_P = (a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))/(2a)
v = (x_P, y_P - a) = (x_P, v_y) where v_y = ( (p-r)(q+R) - a^2 )/(2a)
|v|^2 = x_P^2 + v_y^2

╬╗_E = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2
╬╗_F = R(R+d+r)/|v|^2

Define:
E = (╬╗_E x_P, a(1-╬╗_E) + ╬╗_E y_P) = (╬╗_E x_P, a + ╬╗_E v_y)
F = (╬╗_F x_P, a + ╬╗_F v_y)

B = (0, -a)

Now, we compute the circumcenter O of triangle BEF. We already derived:
D = -2a x_P
X_x = C2/x_P + (╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R))/(4a x_P)
X_y = - (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/(4a)

where C2 = (1/2)(r+R)(d+r+R) + a v_y.

We also have radius^2 = |O-B|^2 = X_x^2 + (X_y + a)^2.

Now, we need to compute the line Ōäō through H parallel to v. H = (x_P, y_H) with y_H = a(d^2 - (R-r)^2)/[2(a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))]. But we can also express y_H in terms of ╬╗_E and ╬╗_F? Note that from earlier, we had y_H = a(d^2 - (R-r)^2)/[2(a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))]. And we also have that a^2 + (p-r)(q+R) =? We can find a relation with v_y. Since v_y = ((p-r)(q+R) - a^2)/(2a), we have (p-r)(q+R) = a^2 + 2a v_y. Then a^2 + (p-r)(q+R) = a^2 + a^2 + 2a v_y = 2a^2 + 2a v_y = 2a(a+v_y). So y_H = a(d^2 - (R-r)^2)/[2 * 2a(a+v_y)] = a(d^2 - (R-r)^2)/(4a(a+v_y)) = (d^2 - (R-r)^2)/(4(a+v_y)). So y_H = (d^2 - (R-r)^2)/(4(a+v_y)). That's a nice simplification.

Thus H = (x_P, (d^2 - (R-r)^2)/(4(a+v_y))).

Now, we need to show that the distance from O to Ōäō equals radius. That is:

|(O-H) ├Ś v| = |v| * radius.

Compute O-H = (X_x - x_P, X_y - y_H). The cross product with v = (x_P, v_y) is:

(O-H) ├Ś v = (X_x - x_P)*v_y - (X_y - y_H)*x_P = v_y X_x - v_y x_P - x_P X_y + x_P y_H = v_y X_x - x_P X_y + x_P y_H - v_y x_P.

Now, we have X_y = - (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/(4a). And we have X_x = C2/x_P + (╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R))/(4a x_P). So compute v_y X_x - x_P X_y = v_y (C2/x_P + (╬╗_E R v_y (d+r+R))/(4a x_P)) - x_P * ( - (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/(4a) ) = v_y C2/x_P + (╬╗_E R v_y^2 (d+r+R))/(4a x_P) + (╬╗_E R x_P (d+r+R))/(4a).

Thus v_y X_x - x_P X_y = v_y C2/x_P + (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/(4a) * ( v_y^2/x_P + x_P ).

Now, the cross product becomes:

(O-H) ├Ś v = v_y C2/x_P + (╬╗_E R (d+r+R))/(4a) * ( v_y^2/x_P + x_P ) + x_P y_H - v_y x_P.

So we need to compute this and compare with |v| * radius. This is messy.

p = - sqrt(r^2 - a^2)
q = sqrt(R^2 - a^2)

But note that r^2 - a^2 = (p^2+a^2) - a^2 = p^2, so sqrt(r^2 - a^2) = |p| = -p (since p negative). So p = -|p|. So that's consistent.

Given the complexity, perhaps we can find a more clever analytic parameterization. Since we have two circles intersecting, we can use the fact that the common chord AB is the radical axis. We can set up coordinates with A and B as (0, a) and (0, -a). Then the circles are given by:

╬®: (x-p)^2 + y^2 = r^2, with r^2 = p^2+a^2.
╬ō: (x-q)^2 + y^2 = R^2, with R^2 = q^2+a^2.

We can also write the equations in the form:

x^2 + y^2 - 2p x + p^2 = r^2 = p^2+a^2 => x^2+y^2 - 2p x = a^2. So ╬®: x^2+y^2 - 2p x = a^2. Similarly, ╬ō: x^2+y^2 - 2q x = a^2. So both circles have the same constant term a^2. So the equations are:

x^2+y^2 - 2p x = a^2
x^2+y^2 - 2q x = a^2

Thus, the circles are defined by these linear equations. So the radical axis is x^2+y^2 - 2p x = x^2+y^2 - 2q x => -2p x = -2q x => (q-p)x=0 => x=0. So the common chord is x=0, which is the y-axis. So A and B are on x=0. So we have A=(0,a), B=(0,-a). Good.

Now, the line MN is the x-axis (y=0). Points C and D are intersections with ╬® and ╬ō: C on ╬® with y=0: x^2 - 2p x = a^2 => x^2 - 2p x - a^2 = 0 => x = p ┬▒ sqrt(p^2+a^2) = p ┬▒ r. Since C is left of M, and M=(p,0), we have x = p - r (since r>0). So C=(p-r,0). Similarly, D=(q+R,0) because D is right of N, and N=(q,0), so x = q + R.

Now, P is circumcenter of triangle ACD. Points: A=(0,a), C=(p-r,0), D=(q+R,0). So C and D on x-axis. The perpendicular bisector of CD is vertical line through midpoint: x = (p-r + q+R)/2 = (p+q+R-r)/2. So P lies on that vertical line: x_P = (p+q+R-r)/2.

Now, we can also find y_P by using the fact that P is equidistant from A and C. So:

(x_P)^2 + (y_P - a)^2 = (x_P - (p-r))^2 + y_P^2.

Expand: x_P^2 + y_P^2 -2a y_P + a^2 = x_P^2 -2x_P(p-r) + (p-r)^2 + y_P^2.

Cancel x_P^2, y_P^2: -2a y_P + a^2 = -2x_P(p-r) + (p-r)^2.

Thus, 2a y_P = a^2 + 2x_P(p-r) - (p-r)^2.

Now, we can compute (p-r)^2 = p^2 -2pr + r^2. But r^2 = p^2+a^2, so (p-r)^2 = p^2 -2pr + p^2+a^2 = 2p^2 + a^2 -2pr.

Then a^2 + 2x_P(p-r) - (p-r)^2 = a^2 + 2x_P(p-r) - (2p^2 + a^2 -2pr) = 2x_P(p-r) - 2p^2 + 2pr = 2x_P(p-r) - 2p(p-r) = 2(p-r)(x_P - p).

Thus, 2a y_P = 2(p-r)(x_P - p) => y_P = (p-r)(x_P - p)/a.

Now, x_P - p = (p+q+R-r)/2 - p = (p+q+R-r-2p)/2 = (q+R-r-p)/2 = ( (q-p) + (R-r) )/2 = (d + (R-r))/2.

So y_P = (p-r)(d+R-r)/(2a). That is a nice expression.

This is a computational approach. I will now attempt to compute the discriminant using the expressions we have, but I will try to simplify using the relations.

LetŌĆÖs define:

We have parameters: p, q, a. We have r = sqrt(p^2+a^2), R = sqrt(q^2+a^2). Also, d = q-p.

We have:

x_P = (p+q+R-r)/2
y_P = (p-r)(d+R-r)/(2a)   (since x_P-p = (q+R-r-p)/2 = (d+R-r)/2)
v = (x_P, y_P - a) = (x_P, v_y) with v_y = (p-r)(d+R-r)/(2a) - a = [ (p-r)(d+R-r) - 2a^2 ]/(2a)

Now, we also have ╬╗_E = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2, ╬╗_F = R(R+d+r)/|v|^2.

Define E = (╬╗_E x_P, a + ╬╗_E v_y), F = (╬╗_F x_P, a + ╬╗_F v_y).

Now, the circle through B=(0,-a), E, F. Let's find its equation.

Let the circle equation be: x^2+y^2 + Dx + Ey + F = 0. Since B lies on it: 0 + a^2 + 0 + E(-a) + F = 0 => a^2 - aE + F = 0 => F = aE - a^2. (1)

Now, plug E: (╬╗_E x_P)^2 + (a+╬╗_E v_y)^2 + D(╬╗_E x_P) + E(a+╬╗_E v_y) + F = 0. (2)
Plug F: (╬╗_F x_P)^2 + (a+╬╗_F v_y)^2 + D(╬╗_F x_P) + E(a+╬╗_F v_y) + F = 0. (3)

We can subtract (2) and (3) to eliminate D and F? Actually, we have two equations with D and E. We can solve for D and E.

LetŌĆÖs denote:

For point E: X_E = ╬╗_E x_P, Y_E = a+╬╗_E v_y.
For point F: X_F = ╬╗_F x_P, Y_F = a+╬╗_F v_y.

Then equations:

X_E^2+Y_E^2 + D X_E + E Y_E + F = 0
X_F^2+Y_F^2 + D X_F + E Y_F + F = 0

Subtract: (X_E^2+Y_E^2 - X_F^2 - Y_F^2) + D(X_E - X_F) + E(Y_E - Y_F) = 0.

So D(X_E - X_F) + E(Y_E - Y_F) = -(X_E^2+Y_E^2 - X_F^2 - Y_F^2). (4)

Now, we also have from (1): F = aE - a^2. Plug into (2): X_E^2+Y_E^2 + D X_E + E Y_E + aE - a^2 = 0 => X_E^2+Y_E^2 - a^2 + D X_E + E(Y_E + a) = 0. (5)

Similarly, from (3): X_F^2+Y_F^2 - a^2 + D X_F + E(Y_F + a) = 0. (6)

Now, we have two linear equations in D and E. We can solve for D and E.

LetŌĆÖs compute some quantities.

First, note that X_E = ╬╗_E x_P, X_F = ╬╗_F x_P. So X_E - X_F = (╬╗_E - ╬╗_F)x_P = - (╬╗_F - ╬╗_E)x_P. And Y_E - Y_F = (a+╬╗_E v_y) - (a+╬╗_F v_y) = (╬╗_E - ╬╗_F)v_y = - (╬╗_F - ╬╗_E)v_y. So (4) becomes: D(- (╬╗_F-╬╗_E)x_P) + E(- (╬╗_F-╬╗_E)v_y) = -(X_E^2+Y_E^2 - X_F^2 - Y_F^2). So (╬╗_F-╬╗_E)(D x_P + E v_y) = X_E^2+Y_E^2 - X_F^2 - Y_F^2. (4')

Now, compute X_E^2+Y_E^2 - X_F^2 - Y_F^2. Since X_E = ╬╗_E x_P, X_F = ╬╗_F x_P, Y_E = a+╬╗_E v_y, Y_F = a+╬╗_F v_y. Then:

X_E^2+Y_E^2 = ╬╗_E^2 x_P^2 + (a+╬╗_E v_y)^2 = ╬╗_E^2 x_P^2 + a^2 + 2a╬╗_E v_y + ╬╗_E^2 v_y^2 = ╬╗_E^2 (x_P^2+v_y^2) + a^2 + 2a╬╗_E v_y = ╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 + a^2 + 2a╬╗_E v_y.

Similarly, X_F^2+Y_F^2 = ╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 + a^2 + 2a╬╗_F v_y.

Thus, X_E^2+Y_E^2 - X_F^2 - Y_F^2 = (╬╗_E^2 - ╬╗_F^2)|v|^2 + 2a v_y (╬╗_E - ╬╗_F) = (╬╗_E-╬╗_F)( (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)|v|^2 + 2a v_y ).

So (4') becomes: (╬╗_F-╬╗_E)(D x_P + E v_y) = (╬╗_E-╬╗_F)( (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)|v|^2 + 2a v_y ) => multiply both sides by -1: (╬╗_E-╬╗_F)(D x_P + E v_y) = (╬╗_E-╬╗_F)( (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)|v|^2 + 2a v_y ). Since ╬╗_E ŌēĀ ╬╗_F (unless r=R? but r<R, so ╬╗_E<╬╗_F), we can cancel (╬╗_E-╬╗_F). Thus:

D x_P + E v_y = (╬╗_E+╬╗_F)|v|^2 + 2a v_y. (4'')

Now, from (5): X_E^2+Y_E^2 - a^2 + D X_E + E(Y_E + a) = 0 => ╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 + 2a╬╗_E v_y + D ╬╗_E x_P + E(a+╬╗_E v_y + a) = ╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 + 2a╬╗_E v_y + D ╬╗_E x_P + E(2a + ╬╗_E v_y) = 0. (5)

Similarly, (6): ╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 + 2a╬╗_F v_y + D ╬╗_F x_P + E(2a + ╬╗_F v_y) = 0. (6)

We have two equations. We can solve for D and E.

LetŌĆÖs denote:

Equation (5): ╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 + 2a╬╗_E v_y + ╬╗_E x_P D + (2a + ╬╗_E v_y)E = 0.
Equation (6): ╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 + 2a╬╗_F v_y + ╬╗_F x_P D + (2a + ╬╗_F v_y)E = 0.

We can treat these as linear in D and E.

LetŌĆÖs write them as:

╬╗_E x_P D + (2a + ╬╗_E v_y)E = -╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_E v_y.   (5')
╬╗_F x_P D + (2a + ╬╗_F v_y)E = -╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_F v_y.   (6')

Now, we can solve for D and E. The denominator of the system is:

╬ö = ╬╗_E x_P * (2a + ╬╗_F v_y) - ╬╗_F x_P * (2a + ╬╗_E v_y) = x_P [ ╬╗_E(2a+╬╗_F v_y) - ╬╗_F(2a+╬╗_E v_y) ] = x_P [ 2a╬╗_E + ╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y - 2a╬╗_F - ╬╗_F ╬╗_E v_y ] = x_P [ 2a(╬╗_E-╬╗_F) ] = 2a x_P (╬╗_E-╬╗_F).

Thus, ╬ö = 2a x_P (╬╗_E-╬╗_F). Since ╬╗_E<╬╗_F, ╬ö is negative.

Now, compute D:

D = ( (-╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_E v_y)*(2a+╬╗_F v_y) - (-╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_F v_y)*(2a+╬╗_E v_y) ) / ╬ö.

LetŌĆÖs denote:

N_D = ( -╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_E v_y)(2a+╬╗_F v_y) + (╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 + 2a╬╗_F v_y)(2a+╬╗_E v_y).

Expand:

First term: (-╬╗_E^2 |v|^2)(2a+╬╗_F v_y) - 2a╬╗_E v_y (2a+╬╗_F v_y) = -2a╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 - ╬╗_E^2 ╬╗_F |v|^2 v_y - 4a^2 ╬╗_E v_y - 2a ╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y^2.

Second term: (╬╗_F^2 |v|^2)(2a+╬╗_E v_y) + 2a╬╗_F v_y (2a+╬╗_E v_y) = 2a╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 + ╬╗_F^2 ╬╗_E |v|^2 v_y + 4a^2 ╬╗_F v_y + 2a ╬╗_F ╬╗_E v_y^2.

Thus, N_D = combine:

Terms with |v|^2: -2a╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 + 2a╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 = 2a(╬╗_F^2 - ╬╗_E^2)|v|^2 = 2a(╬╗_F-╬╗_E)(╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2.
Terms with ╬╗_E^2 ╬╗_F |v|^2 v_y: - ╬╗_E^2 ╬╗_F |v|^2 v_y + ╬╗_F^2 ╬╗_E |v|^2 v_y = ╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 v_y (╬╗_F - ╬╗_E).
Terms with ╬╗_E v_y: -4a^2 ╬╗_E v_y + 4a^2 ╬╗_F v_y = 4a^2 (╬╗_F-╬╗_E) v_y.
Terms with ╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y^2: -2a ╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y^2 + 2a ╬╗_F ╬╗_E v_y^2 = 0.

So N_D = (╬╗_F-╬╗_E)[ 2a(╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 + ╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 v_y + 4a^2 v_y ].

Thus, D = N_D / ╬ö = (╬╗_F-╬╗_E)[ 2a(╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 + ╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 v_y + 4a^2 v_y ] / (2a x_P (╬╗_E-╬╗_F)) = - [ 2a(╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 + ╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 v_y + 4a^2 v_y ] / (2a x_P).

So D = - [ 2a(╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 + ╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 v_y + 4a^2 v_y ] / (2a x_P).

Now, we also need E. Compute E:

E = ( ╬╗_E x_P * (-╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_F v_y) - ╬╗_F x_P * (-╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_E v_y) ) / ╬ö? Actually, from Cramer's rule:

E = ( ╬╗_E x_P * (-╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_F v_y) - (-╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_F v_y) * ╬╗_F x_P ) / ╬ö? Wait, we have system:

A1 D + B1 E = C1
A2 D + B2 E = C2

with A1=╬╗_E x_P, B1=2a+╬╗_E v_y, C1=-╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_E v_y
A2=╬╗_F x_P, B2=2a+╬╗_F v_y, C2=-╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_F v_y

Then E = (A1 C2 - A2 C1) / (A1 B2 - A2 B1) = (╬╗_E x_P C2 - ╬╗_F x_P C1) / (2a x_P (╬╗_E-╬╗_F)) = (╬╗_E C2 - ╬╗_F C1) / (2a (╬╗_E-╬╗_F)).

So E = (╬╗_E C2 - ╬╗_F C1) / (2a (╬╗_E-╬╗_F)).

Now, C1 = -╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_E v_y, C2 = -╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_F v_y.

Thus, ╬╗_E C2 - ╬╗_F C1 = ╬╗_E(-╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_F v_y) - ╬╗_F(-╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 - 2a╬╗_E v_y) = -╬╗_E ╬╗_F^2 |v|^2 - 2a ╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y + ╬╗_F ╬╗_E^2 |v|^2 + 2a ╬╗_F ╬╗_E v_y = ╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 (╬╗_E - ╬╗_F) + 0 = ╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 (╬╗_E-╬╗_F).

Thus, E = [ ╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 (╬╗_E-╬╗_F) ] / [ 2a (╬╗_E-╬╗_F) ] = ╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 / (2a).

So E = (╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2) / (2a).

Now, we have D and E. Also, F = aE - a^2 = a*(╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2/(2a)) - a^2 = (╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2)/2 - a^2.

Thus, the circle equation is:

x^2+y^2 + Dx + Ey + F = 0, with D, E, F as above.

Now, the line Ōäō: X = H + s v, where H = (x_P, y_H) and y_H = (d^2 - (R-r)^2)/(4(a+v_y)). And v = (x_P, v_y). So parametric: x = x_P + s x_P = x_P(1+s), y = y_H + s v_y.

Now, substitute into circle equation:

(x_P(1+s))^2 + (y_H + s v_y)^2 + D x_P(1+s) + E (y_H + s v_y) + F = 0.

This is a quadratic in s: A s^2 + B s + C = 0, where:

A = x_P^2 + v_y^2 = |v|^2.
B = 2 x_P^2 + 2 v_y y_H + D x_P + E v_y.
C = x_P^2 + y_H^2 + D x_P + E y_H + F.

The condition for tangency is that the discriminant ╬ö_s = B^2 - 4 A C = 0.

Now, we can compute B and C in terms of known quantities. Since we have expressions for D and E, and we know that F = aE - a^2, we can simplify.

First, note that |v|^2 = x_P^2+v_y^2.

Also, D = - [ 2a(╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 + ╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 v_y + 4a^2 v_y ] / (2a x_P) = - [ (╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 + (╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 v_y)/(2a) + (4a^2 v_y)/(2a) ] / x_P = - [ (╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 + (╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y |v|^2)/(2a) + 2a v_y ] / x_P.

So D = - [ (╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 + (╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y |v|^2)/(2a) + 2a v_y ] / x_P.

Now, compute B:

B = 2 x_P^2 + 2 v_y y_H + D x_P + E v_y.

Substitute D x_P = - [ (╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 + (╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y |v|^2)/(2a) + 2a v_y ].

So B = 2 x_P^2 + 2 v_y y_H - (╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 - (╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y |v|^2)/(2a) - 2a v_y + E v_y.

Now, E = ╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 / (2a). So E v_y = (╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2 v_y)/(2a). Thus, the terms - (╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y |v|^2)/(2a) + E v_y cancel! So B simplifies to:

B = 2 x_P^2 + 2 v_y y_H - (╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 - 2a v_y.

Now, note that 2 x_P^2 = 2 x_P^2. And we have ╬╗_F+╬╗_E = (r(d+r+R)+R(R+d+r))/|v|^2 = (r d + r^2 + r R + R^2 + R d + R r)/|v|^2 = (d(r+R) + (r+R)^2)/|v|^2 = (r+R)(d+r+R)/|v|^2. So (╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 = (r+R)(d+r+R). Thus, B = 2 x_P^2 + 2 v_y y_H - (r+R)(d+r+R) - 2a v_y.

Now, we also have y_H = (d^2 - (R-r)^2)/(4(a+v_y)). So 2 v_y y_H = 2 v_y * (d^2 - (R-r)^2)/(4(a+v_y)) = v_y (d^2 - (R-r)^2)/(2(a+v_y)).

Thus, B = 2 x_P^2 + v_y (d^2 - (R-r)^2)/(2(a+v_y)) - (r+R)(d+r+R) - 2a v_y.

Now, we also have C = x_P^2 + y_H^2 + D x_P + E y_H + F.

But we know F = aE - a^2. So C = x_P^2 + y_H^2 + D x_P + E y_H + aE - a^2 = x_P^2 + y_H^2 + D x_P + E (y_H + a) - a^2.

Now, D x_P = - [ (╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 + (╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y |v|^2)/(2a) + 2a v_y ] = - (╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 - (╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y |v|^2)/(2a) - 2a v_y.

And E (y_H + a) = (╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2/(2a)) (y_H + a).

So C = x_P^2 + y_H^2 - (╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 - (╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y |v|^2)/(2a) - 2a v_y + (╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2/(2a)) (y_H + a) - a^2.

Now, note that (╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2/(2a)) (y_H + a) - (╬╗_E ╬╗_F v_y |v|^2)/(2a) = (╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2/(2a)) (y_H + a - v_y). So C = x_P^2 + y_H^2 - (╬╗_F+╬╗_E)|v|^2 - 2a v_y + (╬╗_E ╬╗_F |v|^2/(2a)) (y_H + a - v_y) - a^2.

Now, we need to show that B^2 - 4 A C = 0, where A = |v|^2.

This is a computational geometry problem; we can try to do it systematically.

Let's set up coordinates:

Let M = (0,0), N = (d,0). Let ╬®: x^2+y^2 = r^2. ╬ō: (x-d)^2+y^2 = R^2.

Let A = (a, h) with h>0. Then a^2+h^2 = r^2, (a-d)^2+h^2 = R^2.

From these, we derived a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d). And h^2 = r^2 - a^2.

Now define:

p_x = (d+R-r)/2.
p_y = - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h).

We also have v = (p_x - a, p_y - h). Let's compute v explicitly.

First, compute p_x - a = (d+R-r)/2 - a = (d+R-r - 2a)/2.

We know a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d). So 2a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/d. So p_x - a = (d+R-r - (d^2+r^2-R^2)/d)/2 = ( (d(d+R-r) - (d^2+r^2-R^2) )/(2d) ) = ( (d^2+dR-dr - d^2 - r^2 + R^2)/(2d) ) = ( (dR - dr - r^2 + R^2)/(2d) ) = ( (d(R-r) + (R^2 - r^2))/(2d) ) = ( (d(R-r) + (R-r)(R+r))/(2d) ) = ( (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d) ).

So p_x - a = (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d). That's positive since R>r, d>0, R+r>0.

Now compute p_y - h = - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h) - h = - [ (r+a)(d+R-r) + 2h^2 ]/(2h). But we can simplify using h^2 = r^2 - a^2. And also (r+a)(d+R-r) = (r+a)(d+R-r). We might want to express p_y - h in terms of known.

Compute (r+a)(d+R-r) + 2h^2 = (r+a)(d+R-r) + 2(r^2 - a^2) = (r+a)(d+R-r) + 2(r-a)(r+a) = (r+a)[(d+R-r) + 2(r-a)] = (r+a)[d+R-r+2r-2a] = (r+a)[d+R+r-2a].

Thus p_y - h = - (r+a)(d+R+r-2a)/(2h).

Now d+R+r-2a = d+R+r - 2a. But we have a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d). So 2a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/d. Then d+R+r-2a = d+R+r - (d^2+r^2-R^2)/d = (d(d+R+r) - (d^2+r^2-R^2))/d = (d^2+dR+dr - d^2 - r^2 + R^2)/d = (dR+dr - r^2 + R^2)/d = (d(R+r) + (R^2 - r^2))/d = (d(R+r) + (R-r)(R+r))/d = (R+r)(d+R-r)/d.

Thus d+R+r-2a = (R+r)(d+R-r)/d.

So p_y - h = - (r+a) * ((R+r)(d+R-r)/d) / (2h) = - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2dh).

So v = ( v_x, v_y ) where:

v_x = (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d).
v_y = - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2dh).

Now note that v_y is negative (since all factors positive). So v points downward and rightward (v_x positive). So direction of AP is from A to P, which is downward-right.

Now we need t_E = -2(A┬Ęv)/(v┬Ęv). Since A = (a, h). Compute A┬Ęv = a v_x + h v_y. v┬Ęv = v_x^2+v_y^2.

We also need t_F = -2(A-N)┬Ęv/(v┬Ęv). A-N = (a-d, h). So (A-N)┬Ęv = (a-d)v_x + h v_y.

Now we can compute E = A + t_E v, F = A + t_F v.

Now we need B = (a, -h). So we have three points B, E, F. We need to find the circumcircle of triangle BEF. Then show that line through H parallel to v is tangent to that circle.

Let's compute H. H = (p_x, y_H) with y_H = p_x(d-p_x)/p_y.

We have p_x = (d+R-r)/2. d-p_x = d - (d+R-r)/2 = (2d - d - R + r)/2 = (d - R + r)/2. So y_H = p_x * (d-p_x)/p_y = ((d+R-r)/2) * ((d-R+r)/2) / p_y = ((d+R-r)(d-R+r))/(4 p_y).

But p_y = - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h). So p_y negative. Then y_H = ((d+R-r)(d-R+r))/(4 * ( - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h) )) = ((d+R-r)(d-R+r))/(4) * ( -2h/( (r+a)(d+R-r) )) = - (d-R+r) * h / (2(r+a)). Cancel (d+R-r). So y_H = - h (d-R+r) / (2(r+a)).

Now note that d-R+r = d - (R - r). Since d > R - r, this is positive. So y_H negative.

Thus H = ( (d+R-r)/2 , - h (d-R+r)/(2(r+a)) ).

Now we have H and v. The line Ōäō: X = H + s v.

Alternatively, we can compute the power of H with respect to circle (BEF) and then show that the distance from H to the circle along Ōäō is such that the line Ōäō is tangent. Better: For a given line Ōäō through H, the condition that Ōäō is tangent to circle (BEF) is equivalent to: The equation for s when X = H + s v lies on circle has a double root. Another idea: Use coordinate geometry but try to compute the condition for tangency in a more algebraic way, perhaps by showing that the line Ōäō is the polar of H with respect to circle (BEF). Alternatively, we can compute the equation of circle (BEF) and then compute the distance from its center to Ōäō and compare with radius. That is a straightforward but heavy computation. Let's attempt to do it systematically, using algebraic simplifications.

We have parameters: d, r, R. We'll treat them as real numbers with R > r > 0, and R - r < d < R + r.

Define:

a = (d^2 + r^2 - R^2)/(2d).
h^2 = r^2 - a^2.

We also have p_x = (d+R-r)/2.
p_y = - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h).

We have v = (v_x, v_y) with:

v_x = (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d).
v_y = - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2dh).

Now we need t_E = -2(A┬Ęv)/(v┬Ęv). Compute A┬Ęv = a v_x + h v_y.

Compute a v_x = a * (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d). And h v_y = h * ( - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2dh) ) = - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2d). So A┬Ęv = a (R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d) - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2d) = (1/(2d)) [ a(R-r)(d+R+r) - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r) ].

Simplify inside: Let's denote X = a(R-r)(d+R+r) - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r). Expand both terms.

First term: a(R-r)(d+R+r) = a(R-r)d + a(R-r)(R+r) = a d (R-r) + a (R^2 - r^2).

Second term: (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r) = (r+a)(R+r)d + (r+a)(R+r)(R-r) = (r+a)(R+r)d + (r+a)(R^2 - r^2). So X = a d (R-r) + a (R^2 - r^2) - (r+a)(R+r)d - (r+a)(R^2 - r^2) = a d (R-r) - (r+a)(R+r)d + a (R^2 - r^2) - (r+a)(R^2 - r^2) = d[ a(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] + (R^2 - r^2)[ a - (r+a) ] = d[ a(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] + (R^2 - r^2)(-r) = d[ a(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] - r(R^2 - r^2).

Now compute a(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) = aR - a r - (r+a)R - (r+a)r = aR - a r - rR - aR - r^2 - a r = -2a r - rR - r^2? Wait: aR - aR cancel. So we have -a r - rR - a r - r^2? Actually (r+a)(R+r) = rR + r^2 + aR + a r. So a(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) = aR - a r - rR - r^2 - aR - a r = -2a r - rR - r^2. So that simplifies to -r(2a + R + r). So X = d[ -r(2a + R + r) ] - r(R^2 - r^2) = -r d (2a + R + r) - r(R^2 - r^2) = -r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ].

Thus A┬Ęv = (1/(2d)) * ( -r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ] ) = -r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ]/(2d).

Now we need v┬Ęv = v_x^2+v_y^2. Compute v_x^2 = ((R-r)^2 (d+R+r)^2)/(4d^2). v_y^2 = ((r+a)^2 (R+r)^2 (d+R-r)^2)/(4d^2 h^2). So v┬Ęv = (1/(4d^2))[ (R-r)^2 (d+R+r)^2 + (r+a)^2 (R+r)^2 (d+R-r)^2 / h^2 ].

We also need t_E = -2(A┬Ęv)/(v┬Ęv) = -2 * ( -r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ]/(2d) ) / (v┬Ęv) = ( r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ]/d ) / (v┬Ęv) = r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ]/(d v┬Ęv).

So t_E = r[ d(2a+R+r) + (R^2 - r^2) ]/(d v┬Ęv).

Now E = A + t_E v. So coordinates: E = (a + t_E v_x, h + t_E v_y). Similarly, F = A + t_F v, with t_F = -2(A-N)┬Ęv/(v┬Ęv). Compute A-N = (a-d, h). Then (A-N)┬Ęv = (a-d)v_x + h v_y.

Compute (a-d)v_x = (a-d)*(R-r)(d+R+r)/(2d). And h v_y = - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r)/(2d). So (A-N)┬Ęv = (1/(2d))[ (a-d)(R-r)(d+R+r) - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r) ].

Simplify inside: Let Y = (a-d)(R-r)(d+R+r) - (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r). Expand:

First term: (a-d)(R-r)(d+R+r) = (a-d)(R-r)d + (a-d)(R-r)(R+r) = (a-d)d(R-r) + (a-d)(R^2 - r^2).

Second term: (r+a)(R+r)(d+R-r) = (r+a)(R+r)d + (r+a)(R+r)(R-r) = (r+a)(R+r)d + (r+a)(R^2 - r^2).

So Y = (a-d)d(R-r) + (a-d)(R^2 - r^2) - (r+a)(R+r)d - (r+a)(R^2 - r^2) = d[ (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] + (R^2 - r^2)[ (a-d) - (r+a) ] = d[ (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] + (R^2 - r^2)(a-d - r - a) = d[ (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] + (R^2 - r^2)(-d - r) = d[ (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) ] - (R^2 - r^2)(d+r).

Now compute (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r). Expand: (a-d)(R-r) = aR - a r - dR + d r. (r+a)(R+r) = rR + r^2 + aR + a r. So difference = aR - a r - dR + d r - rR - r^2 - aR - a r = -2a r - dR + d r - rR - r^2 = -2a r - dR + d r - rR - r^2. Group terms: = -dR + d r - rR - r^2 - 2a r = d(r-R) - r(R+r) - 2a r = -d(R-r) - r(R+r) - 2a r. So (a-d)(R-r) - (r+a)(R+r) = -[ d(R-r) + r(R+r) + 2a r ].

Thus Y = d * ( -[ d(R-r) + r(R+r) + 2a r ] ) - (R^2 - r^2)(d+r) = -d[ d(R-r) + r(R+r) + 2a r ] - (R-r)(R+r)(d+r) = -d^2(R-r) - d r(R+r) - 2a r d - (R-r)(R+r)(d+r).

So Y = -d^2(R-r) - d r(R+r) - 2a r d - (R^2 - r^2)(d+r).

Thus (A-N)┬Ęv = Y/(2d) = -[ d^2(R-r) + d r(R+r) + 2a r d + (R^2 - r^2)(d+r) ]/(2d).

Now t_F = -2((A-N)┬Ęv)/(v┬Ęv) = -2 * ( -[ ... ]/(2d) ) / (v┬Ęv) = [ ... ]/(d v┬Ęv). So t_F = [ d^2(R-r) + d r(R+r) + 2a r d + (R^2 - r^2)(d+r) ]/(d v┬Ęv).

We can simplify the numerator. Let's denote numerator N_F = d^2(R-r) + d r(R+r) + 2a r d + (R^2 - r^2)(d+r). Note that (R^2 - r^2)(d+r) = (R-r)(R+r)(d+r). So N_F = d^2(R-r) + d r(R+r) + 2a r d + (R-r)(R+r)(d+r). Combine terms with (R-r): d^2(R-r) + (R-r)(R+r)(d+r) = (R-r)[ d^2 + (R+r)(d+r) ] = (R-r)[ d^2 + (R+r)d + (R+r)r ] = (R-r)[ d^2 + d(R+r) + r(R+r) ]. Also we have d r(R+r) + 2a r d = d r(R+r) + 2a r d = d r(R+r + 2a). So N_F = (R-r)[ d^2 + d(R+r) + r(R+r) ] + d r(R+r) + 2a r d.

Now note that a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d). So 2a = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/d. Then 2a r d = r(d^2+r^2-R^2). So N_F = (R-r)[ d^2 + d(R+r) + r(R+r) ] + d r(R+r) + r(d^2+r^2-R^2). Expand (R-r)[ d^2 + d(R+r) + r(R+r) ] = (R-r)d^2 + (R-r)d(R+r) + (R-r)r(R+r) = (R-r)d^2 + d(R^2-r^2) + r(R^2-r^2). So N_F = (R-r)d^2 + d(R^2-r^2) + r(R^2-r^2) + d r(R+r) + r(d^2+r^2-R^2). Combine the terms: d(R^2-r^2) + d r(R+r) = d[(R^2-r^2) + r(R+r)] = d[ R^2 - r^2 + rR + r^2 ] = d(R^2 + rR) = dR(R+r). Also r(R^2-r^2) + r(d^2+r^2-R^2) = r(R^2-r^2 + d^2+r^2-R^2) = r(d^2) = r d^2. So N_F = (R-r)d^2 + dR(R+r) + r d^2 = d^2(R-r + r) + dR(R+r) = d^2 R + dR(R+r) = dR(d + R + r). So N_F = dR(d+R+r). Nice!

Thus t_F = N_F/(d v┬Ęv) = dR(d+R+r)/(d v┬Ęv) = R(d+R+r)/(v┬Ęv).

Given the complexity, maybe we can find a synthetic proof using properties of orthocenter and circumcenter. Let's try to understand the geometry.

We have circles ╬® and ╬ō intersect at A and B. Let M and N be centers. Line MN meets ╬® at C and ╬ō at D, with order C-M-N-D. So C is on ╬® opposite N, D on ╬ō opposite M.

Define P = circumcenter of triangle ACD. So P is the center of circle through A, C, D.

Line AP meets ╬® again at E, and ╬ō again at F.

H is orthocenter of triangle PMN.

Goal: Prove that the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to circumcircle of triangle BEF.

Observations:

- Since M and N are centers, we have MA = MC = r, and NA = ND = R. So M is on perpendicular bisector of AC, and N is on perpendicular bisector of AD. So MP is perpendicular to AC (since P is on perpendicular bisector of AC, and M is also on that line; so line MP is the perpendicular bisector of AC). Similarly, NP is perpendicular bisector of AD.

- So MP Ō¤é AC, NP Ō¤é AD.

- Also, since A, C, D are on circle with center P, we have that P is equidistant from A, C, D. So PA = PC = PD.

- Consider the circle with diameter MN? Not.

- The orthocenter H of triangle PMN: Since M and N are on line MN, the altitude from P is perpendicular to MN. So PH Ō¤é MN. Also, MH Ō¤é PN, NH Ō¤é PM.

- We want to show that the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to circle (BEF). Since B is the reflection of A across MN, and AP is some line, maybe we can show that the line through H parallel to AP is the reflection of the line through H' (some point) parallel to something else.

Maybe we can find that the circle (BEF) is the circle with diameter something like the projection of H onto something. Let's compute the coordinates of E and F in terms of A and P. We have p_x = (d+R-r)/2, p_y = - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h). Let's denote:

U = d+R-r

Then p_x = U/2, p_y = - (r+a)U/(2h). Also, r-a = (R^2 - (d-r)^2)/(2d) = (R-d+r)(R+d-r)/(2d) = (R-d+r)(R+d-r)/(2d). And r+a = (d+r-R)(d+r+R)/(2d).

Now compute |P|^2 = p_x^2+p_y^2 = U^2/4 + (r+a)^2 U^2/(4h^2) = U^2/4 * (1 + (r+a)^2/h^2) = U^2/4 * (2r/(r-a)) = rU^2/(2(r-a)). So |P|^2 = rU^2/(2(r-a)). Then |P|^2 - r^2 = rU^2/(2(r-a)) - r^2 = r[U^2/(2(r-a)) - r] = r[U^2 - 2r(r-a)]/(2(r-a)). So t_E = 1 - r[U^2 - 2r(r-a)]/(2(r-a)). That is t_E = 1 - r(U^2 - 2r(r-a))/(2(r-a)).

Given the complexity, perhaps there is a synthetic proof that is more elegant. Let's try to find a synthetic proof.

We have circles ╬® and ╬ō intersecting at A and B. Let M and N be centers. Let C and D be the intersections of line MN with ╬® and ╬ō respectively, with order C-M-N-D. So C is on ╬® on the side of M opposite N, D on ╬ō on the side of N opposite M.

Define P = circumcenter of triangle ACD. So P is the center of circle (ACD). Note that since M is the center of ╬®, MA = MC = r, so M lies on perpendicular bisector of AC. Similarly, N lies on perpendicular bisector of AD. Thus MP is the perpendicular bisector of AC, and NP is the perpendicular bisector of AD. So MP Ō¤é AC and NP Ō¤é AD.

Now line AP meets ╬® again at E and ╬ō again at F. So A, P, E, F are collinear.

Let H be orthocenter of triangle PMN. Since M and N are on line MN, the altitude from P is perpendicular to MN. So PH Ō¤é MN. Also, MH Ō¤é PN and NH Ō¤é PM.

We need to prove that the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to circumcircle of triangle BEF.

Observation: Since B is the reflection of A across MN, and AP is some line, perhaps the circle (BEF) is the reflection of the circle through A and the two points where the line through P parallel to MN meets the circles? Not.

Another idea: Use the fact that the orthocenter H of triangle PMN is the center of the circle that is the reflection of the circumcircle of PMN across the midpoint of MN? Not.

Maybe we can show that the line through H parallel to AP is the polar of A with respect to the circle (BEF). If we can show that A lies on the polar of H with respect to (BEF), then the line through H parallel to AP is the polar of A? Not.

Let's try to compute the power of A with respect to circle (BEF). Since A, E, F are collinear, and B is symmetric of A, maybe we can find that the circle (BEF) is orthogonal to the circle with diameter AB? Actually, consider the circle with diameter AB. Since AB Ō¤é MN, and MN is the line of centers, the circle with diameter AB has its center at the midpoint of AB, which is on MN. That circle is orthogonal to both ╬® and ╬ō? Not sure.

Given the difficulty, perhaps we can use coordinate geometry with a more clever parameterization. Since we have nice expressions for P, A, etc., maybe we can compute the circle (BEF) and the line Ōäō in terms of d, r, R and then show the tangency condition reduces to an identity. Let's attempt to do that with symbolic algebra, using the fact that we have t_E = 1 - (|P|^2 - r^2) and t_F = 1 - (|P-d|^2 - R^2). We can compute these in terms of d, r, R. We already have |P|^2 = rU^2/(2(r-a)) with U = d+R-r. And we have r-a = (R^2 - (d-r)^2)/(2d) = ((R-d+r)(R+d-r))/(2d). So |P|^2 = rU^2/(2) * (2d)/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) = r d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)). So |P|^2 = r d (d+R-r)^2 / ((R-d+r)(R+d-r)). Then |P|^2 - r^2 = r d (d+R-r)^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) - r^2. That is messy.

But maybe we can find simpler expressions for t_E and t_F using the fact that P is circumcenter of ACD. There might be a relation: The power of P with respect to ╬® is PC^2 - r^2? Actually, P is on perpendicular bisector of AC, so PA = PC. So PC^2 = PA^2. So power of P with respect to ╬® is PA^2 - r^2. That is the same as |P|^2 - r^2? Wait, M is at origin, so |P|^2 = PA^2? Not exactly: PA is distance from P to A, but |P| is distance from P to M. So |P|^2 = PM^2. So power of P with respect to ╬® is PM^2 - r^2. That is not PA^2 - r^2 unless PM = PA. But we have PA = PC = PD, but not necessarily equal to PM. So power_P(╬®) = PM^2 - r^2. And we have t_E = 1 - (PM^2 - r^2). So that's fine.

Similarly, power_P(╬ō) = PN^2 - R^2, and t_F = 1 - (PN^2 - R^2).

Now we can compute PM^2 and PN^2 using coordinates. We have M=(0,0), N=(d,0), P=(p_x,p_y). So PM^2 = p_x^2+p_y^2, PN^2 = (p_x-d)^2+p_y^2. And we have expressions for p_x and p_y in terms of a, h, r, d, R. But we also have a and h expressed in terms of d, r, R. So we can compute PM^2 - r^2 and PN^2 - R^2. Let's do that.

We have:

a = (d^2 + r^2 - R^2)/(2d)
h^2 = r^2 - a^2

p_x = (d+R-r)/2
p_y = - (r+a)(d+R-r)/(2h)

Now compute PM^2 = p_x^2 + p_y^2. We already did: PM^2 = r(d+R-r)^2/(2(r-a)). But we can also compute PM^2 - r^2. Let's compute it in terms of d, r, R.

We have r-a = (R^2 - (d-r)^2)/(2d) = ((R-d+r)(R+d-r))/(2d). So PM^2 = r(d+R-r)^2 * (2d)/(2(r-a)? Actually PM^2 = r d (d+R-r)^2 / ((R-d+r)(R+d-r)). So PM^2 = r d U^2 / (V? Actually (R-d+r) = R - d + r, and (R+d-r) = R + d - r. So PM^2 = r d U^2 / ((R-d+r)(R+d-r)). Then PM^2 - r^2 = r d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) - r^2 = r [ d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) - r ].

Now t_E = 1 - (PM^2 - r^2) = 1 - r [ d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) - r ] = 1 - r d U^2/((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) + r^2.

Similarly, PN^2 = (p_x-d)^2 + p_y^2. p_x-d = (d+R-r)/2 - d = (R-r-d)/2 = -(d+R-r? Actually R-r-d = -(d - R + r) = -V? Where V = d-R+r. So p_x-d = -V/2. Then PN^2 - R^2 = (1/4)[V^2 + (r+a)U^2/(r-a)] - R^2. And t_F = 1 - (PN^2 - R^2) = 1 - (1/4)[V^2 + (r+a)U^2/(r-a)] + R^2 = 1 + R^2 - (1/4)[V^2 + (r+a)U^2/(r-a)].

Now we also have expressions for a, h, etc. Perhaps we can find that t_E and t_F are related to the coordinates of H. H = (p_x, y_H) with y_H = - h (d-R+r)/(2(r+a)) = - h V/(2(r+a)). So y_H = - h V/(2(r+a)). Also, note that V = d-R+r. And U = d+R-r.

|P-M|^2 = (x_P-p)^2 + y_P^2.
But we also have |P-A|^2 = x_P^2 + (y_P-a)^2.
We can express (x_P-p)^2 = (x_P^2 -2p x_P + p^2). So |P-M|^2 = x_P^2 -2p x_P + p^2 + y_P^2.
Thus |P-M|^2 - r^2 = x_P^2 -2p x_P + p^2 + y_P^2 - (p^2+a^2) = x_P^2 -2p x_P + y_P^2 - a^2.
So |P-M|^2 - r^2 = (x_P^2 + y_P^2 - a^2) - 2p x_P.

Now, |v|^2 = x_P^2 + (y_P-a)^2 = x_P^2 + y_P^2 -2a y_P + a^2.
So x_P^2 + y_P^2 = |v|^2 + 2a y_P - a^2.
Thus |P-M|^2 - r^2 = (|v|^2 + 2a y_P - a^2) - a^2 - 2p x_P = |v|^2 + 2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2p x_P.
So ╬╗_E = 1 - (|P-M|^2 - r^2)/|v|^2 = 1 - (|v|^2 + 2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2p x_P)/|v|^2 = 1 - 1 - (2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2p x_P)/|v|^2 = - (2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2p x_P)/|v|^2 = (2a^2 + 2p x_P - 2a y_P)/|v|^2 = 2(a^2 + p x_P - a y_P)/|v|^2.

So ╬╗_E = 2(a^2 + p x_P - a y_P)/|v|^2.

Similarly, we can compute ╬╗_F = 1 - (|P-N|^2 - R^2)/|v|^2. Compute |P-N|^2 = (x_P-q)^2 + y_P^2 = x_P^2 -2q x_P + q^2 + y_P^2. Then |P-N|^2 - R^2 = x_P^2 -2q x_P + q^2 + y_P^2 - (q^2+a^2) = x_P^2 + y_P^2 - a^2 - 2q x_P. Then using x_P^2+y_P^2 = |v|^2 + 2a y_P - a^2, we get |P-N|^2 - R^2 = |v|^2 + 2a y_P - a^2 - a^2 - 2q x_P = |v|^2 + 2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2q x_P. Then ╬╗_F = 1 - (|v|^2 + 2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2q x_P)/|v|^2 = - (2a y_P - 2a^2 - 2q x_P)/|v|^2 = 2(a^2 + q x_P - a y_P)/|v|^2.

Thus we have:

╬╗_E = 2(a^2 + p x_P - a y_P)/|v|^2
╬╗_F = 2(a^2 + q x_P - a y_P)/|v|^2

Now we also have expressions for x_P and y_P in terms of p, q, a, r, R. But we can also express a^2 + p x_P - a y_P and a^2 + q x_P - a y_P in terms of known.

Recall x_P = (p+q+R-r)/2, y_P = [a^2 + (p-r)(q+R)]/(2a). So compute a^2 + p x_P - a y_P = a^2 + p*(p+q+R-r)/2 - a * ([a^2 + (p-r)(q+R)]/(2a)) = a^2 + p(p+q+R-r)/2 - (a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))/2 = a^2 + (p(p+q+R-r) - a^2 - (p-r)(q+R))/2 = a^2 + (p(p+q+R-r) - a^2 - (p-r)(q+R))/2.

Simplify inside: p(p+q+R-r) - (p-r)(q+R) = p^2 + pq + pR - pr - (p(q+R) - r(q+R)) = p^2 + pq + pR - pr - pq - pR + r(q+R) = p^2 - pr + r(q+R) = p(p-r) + r(q+R) = p(p-r) + r(q+R). So then numerator = p(p-r) + r(q+R) - a^2. So a^2 + (p(p-r) + r(q+R) - a^2)/2 = a^2 + (p(p-r) + r(q+R) - a^2)/2 = (2a^2 + p(p-r) + r(q+R) - a^2)/2 = (a^2 + p(p-r) + r(q+R))/2.

Thus a^2 + p x_P - a y_P = (a^2 + p(p-r) + r(q+R))/2.

Similarly, a^2 + q x_P - a y_P = a^2 + q*(p+q+R-r)/2 - (a^2 + (p-r)(q+R))/2 = a^2 + (q(p+q+R-r) - a^2 - (p-r)(q+R))/2 = (2a^2 + q(p+q+R-r) - a^2 - (p-r)(q+R))/2 = (a^2 + q(p+q+R-r) - (p-r)(q+R))/2.

Compute q(p+q+R-r) - (p-r)(q+R) = qp + q^2 + qR - qr - (p(q+R) - r(q+R)) = pq + q^2 + qR - qr - pq - pR + r(q+R) = q^2 + qR - qr - pR + rq + rR = q^2 + qR - pR + rR = q^2 + R(q - p + r) = q^2 + R(d + r) where d = q-p. So then a^2 + q x_P - a y_P = (a^2 + q^2 + R(d+r))/2.

But we can also use the relation R^2 = q^2+a^2. So q^2 = R^2 - a^2. Then a^2 + q^2 + R(d+r) = a^2 + (R^2 - a^2) + R(d+r) = R^2 + R(d+r) = R(R + d + r) = R(R + d + r). So a^2 + q x_P - a y_P = R(R + d + r)/2.

Similarly, for the other expression: a^2 + p x_P - a y_P = (a^2 + p(p-r) + r(q+R))/2. We can also express p(p-r) = p^2 - pr. And r(q+R) = rq + rR. So a^2 + p^2 - pr + rq + rR = (p^2+a^2) - pr + rq + rR = r^2 - pr + rq + rR = r(r - p + q + R) = r(r + q + R - p). So a^2 + p x_P - a y_P = r(r + q + R - p)/2 = r(r + q + R - p)/2. But note that r + q + R - p = (q-p) + (r+R) = d + r + R. So that is r(d+r+R)/2. So a^2 + p x_P - a y_P = r(d+r+R)/2.

Thus we have:

╬╗_E = 2 * (r(d+r+R)/2) / |v|^2 = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2.
╬╗_F = 2 * (R(R+d+r)/2) / |v|^2 = R(R+d+r)/|v|^2.

So ╬╗_E = r(d+r+R)/|v|^2, ╬╗_F = R(R+d+r)/|v|^2.

Now note that |v|^2 = x_P^2 + (y_P-a)^2. We can compute |v|^2 in terms of p, q, a. But maybe we can find a simpler expression. Since we have ╬╗_E and ╬╗_F, we can write:

E = A + ╬╗_E v = (1-╬╗_E)A + ╬╗_E P.
F = A + ╬╗_F v = (1-╬╗_F)A + ╬╗_F P.

Now we also have B = (0, -a). We need to prove that the line through H parallel to v is tangent to circle (BEF). That line is Ōäō: X = H + s v.

Now we can compute the circumcenter O of triangle BEF. Perhaps we can find that O lies on the line through the midpoint of AB? That is the y-axis (x=0). Let's test with numeric. In our earlier numeric, we had p = -0.65, q = 1.85, a = 0.7599. Compute x_P = (p+q+R-r)/2. We need R and r. r = sqrt(p^2+a^2) = sqrt(0.4225+0.5775)= sqrt(1)=1. So r=1. R = sqrt(q^2+a^2)= sqrt(3.4225+0.5775)= sqrt(4)=2. So R=2. Then d = q-p = 1.85 - (-0.65)=2.5. Then x_P = (p+q+R-r)/2 = (-0.65+1.85+2-1)/2 = (2.2)/2=1.1. So x_P=1.1. Then v = (x_P, y_P-a) = (1.1, -3.817-0.7599)= (1.1, -4.5769). |v|^2 = 1.21 + 20.94 = 22.15. So E = A + 0.248v = (0,0.7599)+0.248(1.1,-4.5769)= (0.2728, 0.7599-1.135)= (0.2728, -0.3751). F = A + 0.496v = (0.5456, 0.7599-2.274)= (0.5456, -1.5141). B = (0,-0.7599). We have points: B(0,-0.7599), E(0.2728,-0.3751), F(0.5456,-1.5141). Find perpendicular bisector of BE: midpoint M_BE = (0.1364, -0.5675). Slope BE = (-0.3751+0.7599)/(0.2728-0)=0.3848/0.2728=1.411.
